Banking Sector Deeply Hope the Authorities Calmly Cope with the US Raising Silver Prices, Take Advantage of Domestic Economic Strength to Be Self-Sufficient, Promptly and Properly Plan the Entire Strategy to Stabilize Finance 107

The Xin Xin News Agency reports that after US President Roosevelt implemented raising silver prices this Wednesday (the 10th), the impact caused world silver prices to rise unanimously. Although the local financial market has not yet felt any major impact, the banking sector is deeply concerned about the US government's continuous use of artificial methods to raise silver prices. According to general observation, although the government has taken various measures such as increasing silver export taxes and encouraging the import of foreign silver to stabilize domestic finance, if foreign countries continue to raise silver prices artificially, the continued outflow of domestic silver will be inevitable. Therefore, they deeply hope that the government can calmly cope with this period, take advantage of the domestic economic strength to be self-sufficient, and promptly and properly plan the entire strategy to stabilize finance, so that the foundation of the national economy may not be shaken by foreign threats.

Art Exhibition: Fifth Day of the Preview Exhibition, Qianlong's Imperial Furniture Has Arrived, Renowned Chinese and Foreign Artists Praise It 108

The Central News Agency reports that the Shanghai preview exhibition of the London Exhibition of Chinese Art has been running for five days, from its opening until yesterday. Chinese and foreign individuals, because of the rare opportunity to publicly exhibit these rare collections, have been visiting in the thousands every day. Many arrive in the morning and visit on an empty stomach, and some do not leave until evening. There are also those who visit every day, which shows the greatness of art and the depth of Chinese and foreign people's love for art. A Central News Agency reporter interviewed the person in charge of the exhibition yesterday and learned the following:

Throne Furniture: The Qianlong imperial furniture, stationery, etc. selected by the Palace Museum for the London International Exhibition of Chinese Art have all arrived, including: (1) One rosewood desk, with inscriptions by Liu Yong, Weng Fanggang, etc. carved around the desk; (2) One cloisonné-inlaid throne with clouds and bats, with gilded lacquer footstool; (3) One cloisonné-inlaid screen with scenes of immortal mountains and pavilions, with base; (4) Two bone-tube small writing brushes; (5) One white jade carved pine penholder; (6) One Qianlong-style fish-shaped imperial ink cake; (7) One white jade ink bed, with wooden base; (8) One white jade octagonal ink paste box; (9) Three white jade seals, with wooden box, one engraved with the four characters "Qianlong Chen Han", one engraved with the four characters "Xun Yan Hua An", and one engraved with the five characters "Tu Shu Bi You Yuan"; (10) One Song Chengni stone canal inkstone, with inlaid jade wooden box; (11) One white jade five-sons pen rest, with wooden base; (12) One white jade melon-shaped water holder, with jade spoon; (13) One carved lacquer round box; (14) One Song Ge ware awl-handled bottle, with wooden base; (15) One white jade tube brush, with jade brush cap; (16) One boxwood carved plum blossom armrest, with Xuanzai inscription. The above sixteen items, totaling nineteen pieces, are being sorted and will be displayed publicly in the coming days.

British Community Reception: A group organized by the British community in this port, called the Rotary Club, recently hosted Mr. Hobson, one of the five British commissioners specially sent to China to select antiques. Mr. Hobson gave a long speech on ancient Chinese art, lamenting that it was an exhibition opportunity unseen in thirty years, and also said, "Westerners have a great love for Chinese art, but they are often deceived by clever antique dealers and fail to fully understand Chinese art. Now they can finally see the true face of Mount Lu." A large number of people attended that day, all upper-class British people in Shanghai, and the listeners were all deeply interested.

Preferential Treatment for Groups: The association is offering preferential treatment to academic groups to allow them to glimpse our ancient Chinese art. They are currently formulating preferential treatment methods for academic groups, generally requiring a minimum of ten people and a maximum of twenty-five people per unit. A formal letter of request must be sent to the association, which will arrange the time and schedule for visits. Badges of the group must be worn upon entry. However, Saturdays and Sundays will likely be exceptions.

Famous Artists' Praise: In addition to those in this city, many Westerners have come from afar to visit the exhibition in recent days. Chinese calligraphy and painting masters who visited the exhibition include Xiao Muzhong, Zhao Shuru, Yao Yuqin, Pan Tianshou, Xie Gongzhan, Wang Shengyuan, Shi Chongpeng, Yu Jianhua, Zhang Daqian, Wang Xishen, Wu Hufan, Situ Qiao, Jiang Xiaojian, Guo Chuntao, Zhang Jiong, etc., dozens of people, who believe that the calligraphy and paintings displayed can represent the painting styles of each era, especially the works of Zhong Ju, Fan Kuan, Su, Huang, Mi, and Cai of the Song Dynasty, and Huang, Wang, Ni, and Wu of the Yuan Dynasty, and Shen, Wen, Dong, and Tang of the Ming Dynasty, and the Four Wangs, Wu, and Yun of the Qing Dynasty, which are considered masterpieces. Although they inherited from each other, they have different appearances and each has a unique creative spirit.

Therefore, he suggested setting it at fifty yuan and that shareholders need not be limited to businesses. After Mr. Zhou left, he told a Shiye News Agency reporter, "In addition to raising shares for the Commercial Union Bank, I (Zhou referring to himself) also plan to contact journalists from various places to organize a National Journalists Association. I am scheduled to take the train to Beijing tomorrow night (tonight), stay in Beijing for one to four days, and then return to Shanghai. I am scheduled to take the President Coolidge liner to the United States on the 23rd of this month to inspect overseas Chinese businesses and encourage them to invest in the motherland and develop industries."

Guangdong Chamber of Commerce Requests Assistance

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce yesterday received a letter from Liu Buchi, Executive Committee member of the Guangdong Provincial Federation of Chambers of Commerce, stating: "Dear Sir, it has been noted that our country's economy is declining daily, suffering from the invasion of foreign capital externally and the collapse of the countryside internally. Financial resources are depleted, which is not a matter of a day or two. Recently, due to the global recession and the impact of silver policies, it has suffered an even greater blow. At this critical juncture of survival, there is no way to save the situation without unity and concentration of strength. I have humbly drafted a plan for the Commercial Union Bank, which I have submitted to the Guangdong authorities and the gentlemen of the Guangdong Provincial Federation of Chambers of Commerce, who have adopted it and established a preparatory office to proceed. Its purpose is to unite shops throughout the province, gather strength from many sources, accumulate small amounts into large, in order to establish a powerful financial institution that specializes in the relief of rural areas. Each shop must subscribe to at least one share as a necessary condition, and more subscriptions are welcome. Each share is set at five yuan in national currency. This method is extremely ordinary and the organization is very simple, but its effectiveness can be well-suited to the requirements of the current situation. I respectfully present this to your association in detail. Our country has a vast territory and inconvenient transportation. In addition to large cities, many places have difficulty with remittance and financial activity cannot develop, and a hundred industries have no way to develop. If the Commercial Union Bank is established, then wherever there is a shop, there is the power of the bank. Various methods can be used to connect finance, even in remote areas. Just like the blood vessels of the human body, blood circulation makes the body naturally strong. This is one of its effects. Chinese businessmen have rarely been connected. The establishment of the Commercial Union Bank will unify the will of businessmen and be of great benefit to the future of commercial operations. Furthermore, it can achieve the effect of mutual cooperation and coordination. This is the second effect. The disorder of our country's currency system is known to all. Merchants find it troublesome to transfer funds and suffer intangible losses from repeated calculations. If the Commercial Union Bank is established, it can become a center of finance and a hub of the economy, and gradually improve. This is the third effect. It is undeniable that our country's economy has long been manipulated by the forces of foreign goods. Domestic banks mostly focus on cities, so the decline of the countryside is bound to worsen day by day. If the Commercial Union Bank is established, it will focus on the relief of the countryside, such as running agricultural warehouses and small loans for agricultural workers. The capital of the cities will inevitably return to the countryside, which can not only assist agricultural workers and increase production, but also gradually remove the shackles of foreign capital. This is the fourth effect. The above points are the effects after the establishment of the Commercial Union Bank. Today, the whole country is shaken by the bad environment of recession. All enlightened people regard cooperative business as the only strategy to save the current crisis. The organization of the Commercial Union Bank is a simple and easy way to cooperate in finance. Your association is the leader of chambers of commerce nationwide, and Shanghai is the economic center of the country. If you consider this matter feasible, please grasp the key points and call for a united, large-scale cooperation among the chambers of commerce of all provinces. On the one hand, request the government to grant substantial assistance in order to achieve rapid success. An ancient saying says, 'It is simple at the beginning, but great at the end.' I hope you will carefully consider and pay attention to it (rest omitted)."

National Chamber of Commerce Replies in Agreement

Chairman Lin Kanghou specially replied yesterday, saying: "Dear Sir, I have just received your letter requesting the joint organization of the National Commercial Union Bank. Your great plans are admirable. However, this matter is of great importance and must have a strict organizational law before it can proceed. Otherwise, it will be just empty words and will inevitably lead to failure. If you have any plans, please send them in advance for discussion. As for the subscription of shares, it seems to me that it cannot be based on shops, and five yuan per share is also too fragmented. The minimum should be fifty yuan. I don't know if you agree with my humble opinion. I hereby reply, hoping for your consideration."

Northeast Disabled Soldiers Wang Yamin and Others Petitioned the Party Headquarters Yesterday for Relief; Party Headquarters Sent a Letter to the Public Security Bureau Requesting Repatriation 114

The Da Gong News Agency reports that Wang Yamin, Lin Jingbin, Li Yimin, and 21 other disabled soldiers of Ma Zhanshan's troops were injured and disabled in the Anti-Japanese War. After the war ended, they worked at the Heilongjiang Boji Factory to make a living. Unexpectedly, in March of this year, they were forcibly expelled by Zhang Zhizhu, commander of the puppet army in the area, and escorted to Yingkou, transferred to Tianjin, and disbanded. After arriving in Tianjin, the soldiers searched for their superiors without success. Hearing that Commander-in-Chief Ma Zhanshan had come to Shanghai, they transferred to Shanghai on the 30th of last month to visit and request relief.

Petitioning the Party Headquarters for Relief: After arriving in Shanghai for more than ten days, they found no news and became destitute in Shanghai, unable to maintain their livelihood. At 10 a.m. yesterday, they jointly submitted a document to the Fenglinqiao Municipal Party Headquarters, requesting repatriation. They were received by Yu Yaoqiu, an officer of the Investigation Section, who praised the soldiers' efforts for the country. After consulting the Secretary-General, he agreed to provide assistance with travel expenses and send a letter to the relief agencies for repatriation. The soldiers expressed their gratitude and then withdrew.

Sending a Letter to the Public Security Bureau for Repatriation: After receiving the petition from the disabled soldiers, the Municipal Party Headquarters sent a special letter to the Public Security Bureau yesterday, requesting the issuance of boat tickets for repatriation. The original letter stated, "Dear Sir, we have received a petition from wounded soldiers Wang Yamin and others, stating that they came to Shanghai to visit Commander Ma Zhanshan but did not meet him, and lack funds to return home. Based on this, we have investigated and confirmed that these wounded soldiers are indeed northerners who previously worked hard for the country. This time, because they did not meet the commander, they are destitute in Shanghai, which is very pitiful. We propose that your bureau issue boat tickets at your discretion to assist them in returning home. We hereby send a special letter, hoping you will consider and handle it. This is addressed to the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau." At the same time, they also sent a letter to the Charity Federation, requesting them to provide a subsidy to facilitate their departure.

Dredging the Wusong River: Yujiadun Dam Was Removed Yesterday, Ships Resumed Normal Traffic 115

After the Taihu Lake Water Conservancy Commission dredged the Wusong River and dammed it at Yujiadun, Beishi rice boats had to detour through Nanhuhuangpu for transshipment. Yesterday, the dam was removed, and rice boats can still be transported to Shanghai via the original route. The price of rice in Beishi has shrunk by three corners in the past two days. As for the manure boats, they have also returned to normal. According to a rice boat merchant interviewed by a reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency, when the Taihu Lake Water Conservancy Association closed the dam on April 1st, there was still a route available, but the dredging workers had to charge each boat a transit fee of two yuan, so the boats all detoured. Now that the Water Conservancy Association has announced the resumption of traffic, the traffic of ships has returned to normal.

Chongqing Municipality Various Industries Business Declaration 116

The Shanghai Sichuan Business Association has sent a declaration from various merchants in Chongqing requesting the Sichuan Provincial Government to revise tax regulations. The declaration is recorded as follows: We in Sichuan have long suffered from exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous levies. Officials extract marrow from bones, their desires are insatiable. The people endure the burden with pain, their sweat and blood exhausted. In the past, Sichuan was known as the "Land of Abundance," but now it has become a "Den of Demons." All industries are in decline, the people are struggling to survive, scars are everywhere, and suffering abounds. Fortunately, the Central Government is concerned about the people of Sichuan and has turned its attention westward. The Provincial Government has been reorganized, and administrative reforms are being carried out. At the beginning of its establishment, Chairman Fu Gong immediately announced the abolition of exorbitant taxes and levies to our people, and established local tax bureaus to handle local tax affairs, planning comprehensive and perfect methods to thoroughly eliminate malpractices that harm businesses and the people. We were celebrating the renewal of the tax system, with the hope of seeing the dawn, without the worry of future oppression, and with the expectation of recovery. Unexpectedly, the "One Tax Collection System" issued by the Sichuan Provincial Local Tax Bureau, the content of its tax regulations, was initially kept secret and not clearly announced. Later, due to requests from various guilds, explanations were given to the chambers of commerce, stating that "the assessment standard is not based on customs, but must be based on market prices. Ordinary goods are subject to a 10% export tax and a 15% import tax. Special goods are subject to temporary determination, levied at customs value plus 30% or 20%, or special taxes, etc., in addition to the regular tax, an additional 10% anti-communist suppression fee is added, effective from March 21st." Examining the reduction of the people's burden, it is not about empty words of empathy for business difficulties, but about practice. If the soup is changed but not the medicine, how can the chronic illness gradually improve? Setting up clever names to engage in harsh levies, the pain of the people will inevitably be greater. The "One Tax Collection System" issued by the Local Tax Bureau is, in name, a unified tax system, but in reality, it is the embodiment of exorbitant taxes and levies, becoming more severe and several times greater than in the past. To put it bluntly, it is a tax on top of various exorbitant taxes and levies, plus a suppression fee. (Omitted excerpt)... For the sake of our own survival, for the sake of Chongqing's prosperity, and for the sake of the safety and security of Sichuan's future, we put forward reasonable demands based on conscience and present them to various authorities, requesting relief. For more than ten days, after several appeals, the Provincial Government has slightly changed the regulations for export goods, but the difficulties faced by the wholesale guilds remain the same, without any reduction. Until the end of last month, as a result of face-to-face negotiations between representatives of various guilds and Director Liu of the Finance Department, the following measures were obtained: (1) Each trade association will elect an evaluation committee, together with the local tax bureau, to assess the value of goods, and thereafter taxes will be levied based on the assessed value. (2) For goods already collected but not yet picked up by various guilds, from April 1st, various businesses are allowed to go to the tax bureau with a certificate of responsibility from the trade association to register and pick up the goods. After the price of the goods is assessed, taxes will be paid accordingly. Although the above measures do not provide any real benefits, representatives of various guilds, understanding the government's difficulties, spared no effort to persuade members of their respective associations to endure the pain temporarily. However, members of various guilds believe that this kind of measure has many practical difficulties and even greater invisible harms, and they generally oppose it and do not agree with it. There are thousands of varieties of goods in each guild, with varying prices, making the evaluation extremely difficult. If each item must be listed, the variety is too large. If a second evaluation is required, the procedures are too cumbersome. Moreover, even if members of various guilds follow Director Liu of the Finance Department's measures, and prepare certificates from trade associations and go to pick up goods according to procedures, the tax bureau also refuses to implement it with excuses, and still requires them to pay taxes according to regulations before allowing them to pick up goods. Their lack of sincerity is already imaginable. In our disappointment, we are bewildered, and therefore make the resolution to die, and make the following decisions: 1. The standard for levying taxes on imported goods transported by rotation shall be based on the customs tariff, and no increase shall be allowed. 2. For imported postal packages, the local post office shall collect taxes on behalf of the customs tariff. 3. The tax rate on imported goods shall not exceed 7.5% at most. 4. No additional taxes shall be levied in addition to the regular tax. The above four items are the painful cries we have issued out of necessity. It has been decided by the public that we will resolutely implement them from today onwards, and will not stop until the goal is achieved. This declaration is made by the Chongqing Municipality Cloth and Silk Trade Association, the Suzhou Goods Trade Association, the Dried Vegetables Trade Association, the Hardware and Sundries Trade Association, the Western Medicine Trade Association, the Paper and Printing Trade Association, the Books and Stationery Trade Association, and the Clothing Trade Association, issued on April 10th, Republic of China Year 24.

Cleaners in Hongkou District Initiated Another Strike Yesterday Morning, Resuming Work at Noon After Mediation by the Party Department 117

Cleaners in Zhabei District went on strike the day before yesterday because the contractor Chen Shaofu had not paid their wages for a long time. At the same time, night soil collectors along Qiujiang Road also went on strike due to the same situation. After persuasion by the Party Department, they resumed work at noon. Unexpectedly, at around 5 a.m. yesterday, 116 night soil collectors in the Xingjia Muqiao area of Hongkou District went on strike again from 6 a.m. because the contractor Ma Leming's whereabouts were still unknown, and the middle-level staff hid and refused to meet them, without any guarantee for their unpaid wages. After hearing the news, the District Cleaners' Union sent personnel to dissuade them, but to no avail. They then sent Xu Xuecheng, Wu Zhilai, Guan Yian, and others to the Municipal Party Department to report and ask for instructions. The Municipal Party Department then sent Lu Yinchu to persuade them, and at the same time went to the Finance Bureau to discuss solutions with Section Chief Wang of the Bureau's Second Section, and staff member Ni. As a result, it was decided that the Finance Bureau would be responsible for recovering the arrears from the contractor's guarantor and paying them all within three days. All the workers were satisfied and resumed work at around 11 a.m.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Presents to the Ministry, Striving for Hong Kong Passenger Permits 121

The "Si Hai" ship, built with Sino-British Boxer Indemnity funds, and the "Hai Yuan" ship employ foreigners as the chief and second mates, chief engineer, and chief and second assistant engineers. Therefore, Hong Kong granted passenger permits. However, the "Hai Heng," "Hai Li," and "Hai Zhen" ships were refused passenger permits because they employed Chinese crew members. Because of its status as a state-run company, the company was unwilling to compromise or hire all foreign crew members. Therefore, it abandoned Hong Kong passenger permits for the three ships and requested the Central Government to negotiate. However, the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Board of Directors asked the Ministry of Communications, as the three "Hai" ships did not carry Hong Kong passengers, causing significant business losses and not in line with the original agreement. The Ministry of Communications forwarded the inquiry to the company. As a result, it was found that abandoning Hong Kong passengers for the three ships caused an annual loss of more than 50,000 yuan. If foreign crew members were hired instead, the salary expenses would also increase by more than 20,000 yuan, resulting in an actual loss of only more than 20,000 yuan. However, this would cause significant damage to national prestige and sovereignty, which is difficult to compromise. Hong Kong and Kowloon are ceded territories, so it is not possible to ask the Hong Kong authorities to recognize our crew certificates. After discussion, the company has submitted a request to the Ministry of Communications to forward it to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, requesting that a special commissioner be dispatched to the UK to negotiate with the British government, striving for them to order the Hong Kong government to recognize the validity of our country's crew certificates and grant passenger permits to allow for the carrying of Hong Kong passengers. The submission was sent to Beijing yesterday.

Import and Export of Radio Materials, Allowed with Ministry of Communications Registration Certificate, No Need to Obtain Transit Permit Again 125

Tang Hai'an, Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, and Luo Fude, Commissioner of Customs, have added Article 7 to the Provisional Measures for Applying for Transit Permits for Radio Materials. They posted a joint proclamation yesterday, stating that the matter of radio materials being transported for transit should require a transit permit. On December 10th of last year, Announcement No. 1407 was issued. Now, the Customs Administration of the Ministry of Finance has ordered that a new article, namely Article 7, be added to the Provisional Measures for Applying for Transit Permits for Radio Materials. The text of the article is as follows: "Each household registered with the Ministry of Communications for broadcasting radios is allowed to carry the originally registered radio for travel or repair by presenting the registration certificate issued by the Ministry of Communications for inspection and release, without the need to obtain a transit permit again." It is ordered that this be known, so that all merchants are aware. This announcement is hereby made.

Man and Woman Take Poison Over Marriage 132

At around 10 PM the night before last, a well-dressed young man and a woman in a gray silk cheongsam suddenly came to the Da Hu Hotel west of East Xinqiao on Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession. They opened room 220 on the second floor and paid a deposit of two yuan. On the registration book, they signed Chen Shanchang, 24 years old, from Guangdong, currently working at the Nanyang Tobacco Company, and Li Suqin, 17 years old, also from Guangdong. After entering the room, the two immediately closed the door and went to bed. Unexpectedly, at around 9 AM yesterday morning, the duty tea boy suddenly heard moaning sounds from the room, so he pushed open the door and entered. He saw the two hugging each other tightly, lying on their backs on the bed, their faces pale. He knew that they had taken poison and found a Snowflake Cream bottle on the table, containing a small amount of opium. He immediately reported it to the police station. The head of the police sent detectives to investigate, then sent them to Renji Hospital for treatment. Two suicide notes were found beside the two. One was written by the man, addressed to Liu Tao at No. 147 Heping Lane, Baibolu Road, North Sichuan Road. The letter stated that he had committed suicide, please inform his mother, and don't be sad. He only asked that they be buried in the same grave after death. The letter was signed Zheng Jia at the end. The other letter was written by the woman, addressed to her widowed mother at No. 573 West Wuchang Road, Dean Grocery Store, stating that because of her unreasonable oppression and the destruction of the marriage, she had no choice but to die. However, after the doctors administered an enema, the two were out of danger. After further rest, they can recover their health.

The Sunken Lin Xing Wheel Has Started Service Again, and the Body of the Captain Has Been Recovered 133

The "Lin Xing" towed barge of the Songhu Maoxing Company was sunk by the "Xin Shuntai" small vessel outside Sanxia Shuikou at 10:30 PM on March 14th due to a dispute over business. The captain, Huang Helou, fell into the water with the ship and drowned. The Fourth Squad of the Water Patrol detained the two crew members of the "Xin Shuntai" who caused the accident and sent them to the Shanghai Local Court for questioning. The shipwreck's location was found by the Hydrographic Survey Bureau. The details have been reported repeatedly in this newspaper. It is learned that after Maoxing Company learned the location of the sunken ship, fearing it would obstruct the navigation route, it hired workers to salvage it at a cost of 350 yuan. After the ship was salvaged, Maoxing Company sent personnel to inspect and found that the hull of the "Lin Xing" was made of iron, so it was not severely damaged. The damaged parts were only the bridge and various equipment on the deck, which required repair costs of more than 2,000 yuan. Therefore, they immediately hired workers in Songhu to repair it, which has been completed. It has started service again yesterday. However, the negotiation and compensation issue with "Xin Shuntai" will be determined by the court's judgment. The body of Huang Helou has also been recovered. After verification by the company, the coffin was temporarily placed in the Siming Guild Hall in Wusong, and will be transported back to its original home for burial after the issue is resolved.

Fire at Oil Shop on Wuzhen Road, Losses of 7-8,000 Yuan 134

A fire broke out at the Ruitai Oil Shop at No. 15-17 Wuzhen Road Bridge in Zhabei at 10:45 AM yesterday. The shop happened to be located south of the Wuzhen Road Police Station of the Xinzha Branch Bureau, separated by only three storefronts, so Inspector Luo Siwei immediately called the Fire Brigade after hearing the alarm and sent a leather hose truck to the scene for rescue. On the one hand, he led the patrol police to maintain order. After the fire brigades made every effort to put out the fire, it was extinguished at 11:05 AM. It is estimated that two rooms of the shop's building were destroyed, and the roof was not penetrated. Afterwards, the police station arrested the arsonist, Gu Chengchu, 35 years old, from Jiading, who confessed that he was the accountant in the oil shop. The boss, Pan Ruifu, was not in the shop. The cause of the fire was that the old servant Cao Tonggen (from Tongzhou) was opening an oil barrel, and the screw had rusted. He hit it with an iron hammer, and sparks flew out and entered the oil, causing the disaster. Cao Tonggen has now fled, and the other apprentices are unknown. About 4-500 cans of kerosene, diesel, motor oil, machine oil, etc. were burned, with a total loss of 7-8,000 yuan including the shop's foundation, excluding the house. The shop did not have fire insurance. After verifying the confession, Inspector Luo sent him to the Xinzha Branch Bureau, and Bureau member Ouyang Liu, after clarifying the previous situation, ordered him to be sent to the Third Section of the Public Security Bureau for disposal.

Feud Over Taking Over Kettle Shop, Wang Wenyao Was Killed, Perpetrator Detained Pending Trial 135

The kettle shop at No. 208 Longhua Road, Nanshi, was previously leased by Wang Zuoju from Anhui. Recently, the original owner took it back and leased it to Wang Wenyao (40 years old) from Nanjing to take over. Afterwards, Wang Wenyao's wife, Ms. Yang (30 years old), took the injured person by car to Shanghai Hospital for treatment. On the one hand, she reported the situation to the police station in charge and dispatched police to Julu Road, arrested Wang Zuoju, the uncle of Wang Xiaoheshang, and arrested Zhang (24 years old, from Tianjin), the wife of Wang Zhenbiao, and another accomplice, Fei Dequan (24 years old, from Anhui), at No. 198 Longhua Road. First, the victim's wife, Wang Yang, testified as described above and requested redress. Next, Wang Zuoju, Fei Dequan, and Wang Zhang, etc., gave evasive statements. At this point, Prosecutor Wu Deying came to court to present his opinion, followed by the lawyer Hu Yuanjun, hired by the defendants, who defended them. The judge considered it concluded and scheduled the judgment for the 18th of this month. The three defendants were returned to custody to await further instructions.

Official Order for Party and Government Organizations to Form a People's Common Sense Guidance Committee; Decision Made to Appoint Representatives from 29 Organizations as Committee Members; Articles of Association for the People's Common Sense Guidance Committee Approved 136

The Shanghai Special Municipality Party Headquarters, recently acting upon orders from the Central Government, convened various organizations and groups in the city to prepare for the establishment of the People's Common Sense Guidance Committee. Yesterday afternoon at 2 PM, the inaugural meeting was held at the conference room of the Chinese Academic Society, where committee members were determined and the articles of association were revised and approved. Details are recorded as follows:

Attending Organizations: Included representatives from the Municipal Party Headquarters (Lin Meiyan, Wang Longzhang, Yu Zhongbiao), the Municipal Government (Xiang Yusi), the Garrison Command (Wang Pixian), the Bureau of Health (Hu Weizhi), the Bureau of Education (Sun Yucai), the Bureau of Public Safety (Jin Zhongjian), the Bureau of Social Affairs (Ma Zhiqian), the Chinese Vocational Education Society (Jiang Wenyu), the Lawyers Association (Shen Junru), the Physicians Association (Guo Yuyuan), the Municipal Education Association (Zhang Lichun), the People's Education Center (Cao Jingxian), the Municipal Farmers Association (Yu Zhenhui), the Chinese Academic Society (Wei Zhaoji), the Modern Thought Society (Chen Weifan), the Shanghai Machinery Industry Association (Cheng Shouzhong), the Shanghai Branch of the Cultural Construction Association (Huang Jingzhai), the Social Education Society (Lu Hailan), and dozens of others.

Chairman's Report: The meeting was chaired by Lin Meiyan from the Municipal Party Headquarters, with Wang Longzhang serving as the recorder. Following ceremonial formalities, the chairman reported, stating in brief: "Recently, the Municipal Party Headquarters received orders from the Central Government to organize the People's Common Sense Guidance Committee in this municipality. This is significant because statistics show that illiteracy among the Chinese people nationwide is as high as 80%. Shanghai, as a culturally concentrated area with a population of 3.5 million, also has 500,000 illiterate individuals. The Central Government is both working to eliminate illiteracy and finding ways to instill common sense about hygiene, society, politics, etc., among the people, so as to promote social progress and ensure personal safety. The Central Government has already stipulated the guidelines for this Guidance Committee, which is to be jointly organized by various organizations and groups, and its work has also been detailed. The reason for convening this meeting today is precisely this."

Discussion of Proposals: After the chairman's report, the discussion of proposals began. (1) Yu Zhenhui proposed that the meeting be formally declared an establishment meeting, which was unanimously approved by all representatives and resolved. (2) The Articles of Association of the People's Common Sense Guidance Committee were discussed and resolved to be revised and approved (the Articles of Association are attached). (3) The location of the committee was determined, and it was resolved that the chairman would be responsible for finding a suitable location. (4) It was resolved that the committee would send letters to various organizations requesting them to nominate fixed representatives as committee members, which was passed. (5) The next meeting date was set for 2 PM on the 26th of this month, and the meeting adjourned.

Approved Articles of Association: The following Articles of Association of the Shanghai Municipal People's Common Sense Guidance Committee were approved: (1) The purpose of this committee is to instill common sense in the people, enhance their self-reliance, and promote the completion of political tutelage. (2) This committee will be composed of one fixed representative each from the following 29 organizations: Shanghai Municipal Party Headquarters, Songhu Garrison Command, Shanghai Municipal Government, Bureau of Education, Bureau of Social Affairs, Bureau of Health, Bureau of Public Safety, Municipal Education Association, Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Municipal General Labor Union, Municipal Farmers Association, Physicians Association, Lawyers Association, Daily Newspaper Association, Journalists Association, Academia Sinica, Shanghai Branch of the Chinese Cultural Construction Association, Chinese Academic Society, Chinese Vocational Education Society, Shanghai Social Education Society, Modern Thought Society, People's Education Center, China Chemical Industry Federation, Machinery Industry Association, Federation of Charitable Organizations, Municipal Women's Association, People's Literacy Movement Guidance Committee, Certified Public Accountants Association, and the Shanghai Branch of the Chinese Scientific Movement Association. The representative from the Municipal Party Headquarters will serve as the chairman of the committee and be responsible for convening meetings. (3) All committee members of this committee will serve without pay. (4) This committee may establish various subcommittees depending on the amount of work involved, and the chairman of the committee will propose candidates for appointment, subject to approval by this committee. (5) This committee will have one executive director responsible for planning the work, who will be appointed by the chairman of the committee and serve without pay. (6) This committee will have several staff members who will be seconded from party and government organizations as appropriate, and their travel expenses will be borne by their respective organizations. (7) The expenses of this committee will be borne by the party and government organizations as appropriate. (8) This committee will meet once a month, and the chairman of the committee may convene temporary meetings when necessary.

Guidance Items: (6) The guiding principles of this committee are temporarily set as follows: A. Concerning the promotion of party ideology, the training of gatherings, and instructions for family and child management. B. Concerning reports on the latest domestic and international military and political situations, explanations of laws and regulations, and the implementation of local government orders. C. Concerning the inculcation of military knowledge, technical demonstrations, and anti-aircraft drills. D. Concerning health education, fire prevention, and the maintenance of public order. E. Concerning the guidance of agricultural and sideline industries and handicrafts in terms of improvement, marketing, and storage methods. F. Concerning instructions on commercial ethics, product selection, and general commercial knowledge. G. Concerning explanations and experiments on simple physics, chemistry, and natural phenomena. H. Concerning instructions on the deeds of native sages, martyrs, creators, academics, and special national figures. I. Concerning instructions on all kinds of common transportation knowledge and rules to be followed. J. Concerning instructions on the deeds of meritorious figures from around the world.

Guidance Methods: The guidance methods of this committee are provisionally set as follows: A. Lectures, B. Movies, C. Experiments, D. Exhibitions, E. Recreation, F. Publishing books, G. Posting pictures and slogans, H. Creating common sense guidance signs, I. Others. (11) This committee may accept public inquiries on various issues and provide detailed answers, and publish them in newspapers when necessary. (12) When necessary, this committee may request assistance from relevant competent authorities or organizations for guidance or answers on various types of common sense. (13) This committee should compile a weekly work report summarizing its activities and submit it to the Municipal Party Headquarters for forwarding to the Central People's Movement Guidance Committee for record. (14) This committee is a permanent body, but the Municipal Party Headquarters may order its reorganization when deemed necessary. (15) These Articles of Association may be amended if there are any unaddressed matters. (16) These Articles of Association will be implemented after being approved by this committee and submitted to the Municipal Party Headquarters for record.

Kidnapper Zheng Tangsheng Sentenced to Death After Appeal; Shang, Liu, and Wu Changed to Life Imprisonment; Zheng's Elderly Father, Wives and Concubines All Wept Silently 137

Jin Jiulin, Inspector of the Special Agency of the French Concession Police Department, along with detectives Zhang Ziying, Zhou Bingcheng, etc., successively arrested renowned ringleader of kidnapping giant bandits and suspects Zheng Tangsheng, Shang Zhen, Liu Yimin, Wu Shaoting, Geng Huatang, Li Yueshan, Yu Yuanzhou, Chang Jianxi, Bian Zenghua, Wang Shikong, Fang Qingshan, and woman Zheng Chen (Zheng Tangsheng's concubine, formerly a prostitute) and other men and women, twelve in total, in the Japanese Concession of Tianjin and elsewhere on July 25, 1933. They were transferred to Shanghai, where it was discovered that they had successively kidnapped Huang Yuyi, Vice President of the Zhongnan Bank; Chen Yanghe, Assistant Manager of the Si Ming Bank; He Shaoting, owner of the Xin Sen Ji Construction Factory; Gu Zelin, son of Yunnan Division Commander, etc.; and wealthy timber merchant Huang Baohua, extorting huge sums as ransom in Tianjin and Shanghai. They were also involved in the murder of Xiaoshaoxing, a member of their gang, and the kidnapping of Chen Zhuling and Liang Huiwu, Compradors of the Jardine Matheson Company in Tianjin.

Kidnapping and tearing up the tickets, burying corpses to destroy evidence and other major cases. They were handed over to the Second Special Court for public prosecution under the Regulations for the Punishment of Bandits. Because no criminal behavior was found on Zheng's concubine, Chen, she was not prosecuted and was first released. After investigation and trial, Zheng and the other eleven were sentenced on October 14 of the same year. Zheng Tangsheng, Shang Zhen, Liu Yimin, and Wu Shaoting were each sentenced to death and deprived of their public rights for life. Li Yueshan was sentenced to fifteen years in prison. Yu Yuanzhou, Chang Jianxi, Bian Zenghua, Wang Shikong, and Fang Qingshan were declared innocent. Geng Huatang, because he feared punishment, committed suicide in the detention center of the police department during the period awaiting judgment.

The public prosecution was not accepted for review. Afterwards, Zheng, Shang, Liu, and Wu appealed against the original judgment and requested approval from the Jiangsu Provincial Government to have the case sent back for retrial. After repeated court sessions and investigations by Wang Gangxu, the Presiding Judge of the Criminal Division of the Second Special Court, and investigations were conducted with various agencies, organizations and Putuo Mountain Baobentang temples, etc., and all details were sought. After a year and a half, twelve court sessions were held. Although the defendants overturned their original confessions, denied participation in the kidnapping, and hired lawyers to defend them, they were ultimately found guilty based on conclusive evidence, making it impossible to conceal the facts. The debate was declared concluded on the 7th of this month, and a date was set for announcing the verdicts, as reported in detail in previous reports. Yesterday was the date for the pronouncement of the verdicts. At around 10 AM, Judge Wang, accompanied by clerk Zheng Rong, arrived at Criminal Court One, ordered Zheng and the other four defendants to be brought before the court. After a brief inquiry into their ages and origins, he

Announced the Judgment: Except for Zheng, the original sentence was upheld. Shang, Liu, and Wu's original sentences were revoked, and the principal sentence was re-sentenced: Zheng Tangsheng was sentenced to death for repeatedly helping to kidnap and extort ransom, and deprived of his public rights for life; Receiving stolen goods (referring to the ransom money received) was sentenced to two years of imprisonment. The death sentence was carried out and deprived of his public rights for life. Shang Zhen was sentenced to life imprisonment for continuing to help kidnap and extort ransom and deprived of his public rights for life. Liu Yimin and Wu Shaoting were each sentenced to life imprisonment for repeatedly helping to kidnap and extort ransom and deprived of their public rights for life; Conspiracy to commit murder was sentenced to six years of imprisonment. Each of them will be executed for life imprisonment, deprived of his public rights for life. When Zheng and others heard the verdict, they all bowed their heads silently. When the bailiff took them back to the prison, only Zheng's elderly father and his wife brought Zheng's eldest son (over ten years old) and four-year-old child, and Zheng's concubine, Chen, etc.

Wept in Silence While watching Zheng being taken back into custody. When they went to the detention center to visit and comfort him, Zheng shouted from inside the iron bars of the prison to his father, wives, concubines, and beloved sons, telling them not to be sad, and saying that everyone in the world inevitably dies, and since he had committed a crime, he had no regrets about dying, but he hoped that his relatives and friends would take care of his elderly father, wives, and concubines, seek a stable life, cultivate his two sons, and study hard so that they could serve the country in the future. A dying man's words are good, and a dying bird's song is sad, which made the bystanders feel sympathetic and compassionate. The major kidnapping case that shocked both Tianjin and Shanghai has also come to an end. It is also heard that Shang, Liu, and Wu also committed similar cases in the Public Concession. Because the Second Special Court had already sentenced them to death at that time, they did not request the transfer for trial. Now that the Second Special Court's retrial has resulted in the three defendants being sentenced to life imprisonment, it is feared that they will request the transfer for trial in the future.

On June 18, 1933, at approximately 1 AM, Wang Xinggao, a native of Funing, the mastermind behind the assassination of Tang Jiapeng, the former manager of the Great World, escaped and remained at large. Liang Su, a Cantonese man, aged forty, the head clerk of the Guang Yu Rong Customs Brokerage firm at 212 North Jiangxi Road, had been working for the firm for many years. The previous morning at 10:30 AM, manager Chen Tianzi instructed him to take a draft of four hundred and ten dollars from the Shanghai Bank Hongkou Branch and a draft of fifty dollars from the China Industrial Bank to collect cash, as the other employees of the firm were out conducting business. He first went to the Shanghai Bank and collected the money as requested. However, after obtaining this large sum of money, he suddenly had a wild idea and went to the gambling den at Sanduoli in the Chinese territory on North Sichuan Road to make a final gamble, hoping to get lucky. However, Heaven did not grant his wish, and he lost everything. In a moment of desperation, Liang decided to go all in and rushed to the Industrial Bank to collect another fifty dollars in Yuan coins, intending to launch another battle. However, the money was to be paid to Mr. Tong, a Hakka, who had insufficient deposits and was returned. Liang immediately fled to his home at No. 100 Siwenli on the Great World Bend Road, trying to figure out a solution. By noon, manager Chen realized that Liang had not returned and feared that something had happened, so he went to both banks to investigate and discovered the incident. He immediately reported it to the Hongkou Police Department, which dispatched detective Feng Qi to investigate. He secretly went to Liang's home and arrested him, taking him to the police station. The defendant Liang was sent to the Criminal Court Three of the First Special Court yesterday morning. Young Woman Sues Mother for Seizing Inheritance 140

Li Weici, a young woman residing in a village, 25 years old, recently filed a lawsuit in the local court against her birth mother, Li Qiao, accusing her of obstructing her inheritance, requesting a judgment to order an appropriate allocation. The gist of her lawsuit is as follows: "When my father, Li Luji, passed away, I was only eight years old, and I married at the age of twenty-three. My father, during his lifetime, had an affair with a woman named Xu from a iron shop in this town. My father was very fond of the plaintiff and sent her to school from an early age, giving her higher education, hoping that she would be no different from men. Before his death, he also instructed my birth mother to give me property, repeatedly urging her to give the plaintiff four tenths of the inheritance." After the court accepted the case, Judge Sun Jikang opened the court yesterday morning and summoned the parties for trial. The plaintiff, Li Weici, appeared in court with her lawyer, Wang Rumei. The defendant, Li Qiao, and Li Xu also appeared in court with their lawyer, Zhou Ziying, to present their defense. First, Li Weici testified to the previous events, followed by Li Qiao, who testified that she was 48 years old and that when her husband passed away, he did say that four tenths of the property should be given to the plaintiff, but if it were given all at once, it would affect our future lives. The official asked about the amount of property, and she replied that there were over 120 mu of land and four houses. The official asked how much each mu was worth, and she replied that it was about 50 yuan. Finally, Li Xu testified that she was 28 years old, was Li Luji's concubine, and had a son named Da Ren, who was seventeen years old. All of the late husband's inheritance should be inherited by my son. What evidence does the plaintiff have to request the distribution of the inheritance this time? I do not want to analyze it now, please investigate. The official received the testimony, instructing the plaintiff to pay the litigation fees and then schedule another joint hearing.

This association will send Hu Yuantang together with Hu Jiepu, the representative from Jixi, to collect the funds from Hu Xiangjun. Resolution: This association will send Mr. Shao Shuwei to Jixi to assist in the handling and to be responsible for reporting back. Matters related to public welfare should all be voluntary. (4) Jixi County Magistrate Chen Bikui and county gentry Hu Yunchong sent a telegram requesting the purchase of rice for cheap sale due to the banditry and drought disasters in Jixi, please review the proposal. Resolution: To be handled together with the case. (5) Jixi County Magistrate Chen and the Post-Disaster Committee sent a letter requesting disaster relief, and sent Hu Jiepu and Hu Xiangzhao to Shanghai to solicit donations for the purchase of rice for cheap sale. Resolution: In addition to the more than 1,000 yuan donated at that time, the various merchants will be invited to solicit donations on the same date. (6) For the Ge Changhe Creditors and Debtors Clearance Committee, if there are any dealings with fellow villagers, please register the case. Resolution: To notify all members. (7) Shao He sent a letter requesting that refugee Zhang Jinhe be sent back to his hometown. Resolution: To be handled accordingly. Resolution: A letter will be sent to Feng Xucheng, Rong Ruichang, Hu Xingyao, Xiao Xiaoren, Liu Xinquan, Zhao Xianji, Hou Yehua, and You Rongbo as ballot counting assistants. (1) Discussed and resolved the date for reopening the ballot. Resolution: April 14th at 9:00 AM.

Wu Xiahu Asks Ganpu Fellow-Villagers to Provide Disaster Relief 148

Ganpu, Zhejiang, suffered a severe drought last year. This spring, flowers, fruits, beans, and wheat were hit by frost, rain, and snow, making the people even more impoverished. Wu Xiahu of the town wrote a letter to his fellow villagers, saying: "Since our Ganpu suffered a rice pest infestation in the eleventh year of the Republic of China, years of famine have followed, and the burden is extremely heavy. The people have nothing to cover themselves with. Last year, we suffered the most severe drought, and the disaster situation was so tragic that it cannot be fully described in words or with pen and ink. Although Mr. Lu Bohong, Chen Jiongwen, Wu Linkun, Cheng Fupi, Chen Peiyuan, Zhou Xinbo, Bu Bosun, Wang Shenfu, Zhou Shuyuan, Zhao Wenxiang and others have worked together to provide disaster relief, it is still insufficient. Furthermore, the spring flowers that farmers were hoping for a bumper harvest have now been almost completely destroyed by frost. Now, the farmers have no strength to plant seeds, and more than 30,000 disaster victims are crying out for food. The rural and urban areas are closely related. Please, fellow villagers, quickly rise up to provide disaster relief!"

Records of the Petition by Workers of the Shēn Xīn Mill No. 5 149

The entire body of workers from Shēn Xīn Mill No. 5, organized as a petition delegation for resumption of work, dispatched representatives Zhao Yún, Jì Fúlín, Yú Lǔquán, Wáng Jīnshēng, and others at 10:30 AM on the 10th of this month, bearing a written petition to the Municipal Government. They were received by Yú Míngdé of the Second Section. The representatives stated that since the closure of Mill No. 5, the general workers had pawned everything they owned and exhausted their savings, suffering from hunger and cold to an unbearable degree. If the Municipal Government could not find a solution, the workers, having waited for too long, could no longer endure it and feared that incidents would occur. They also requested a prompt reply from the Municipal Government. Mr. Yú expressed that the Mayor was already aware of the workers' suffering and had instructed the Social Affairs Bureau to handle the matter quickly, assuring that the Bureau was not being negligent. The Social Affairs Bureau had already submitted a document requesting the Mayor's approval, and it was hoped that the factory could be reopened. At most, a concrete response would be given in four days, and the representatives were asked to return and reassure the workers.

Zhāng Ān Reduces Fees to Aid Disaster Relief 151

Zhāng Dàn'ān of Lánlíng has meticulously studied the eight styles of calligraphy for over thirty years, deeply grasping the essence of the art. His clerical script is ancient, vigorous, and elegant, drawing inspiration from the Qin and Han dynasties, distinct from contemporary vulgar styles. In recent years, he traveled extensively, and famous officials and dignitaries in various provinces eagerly sought his company. Moreover, Mr. Zhāng is naturally kind, generous, and philanthropic, always taking the lead in charitable endeavors and gladly supporting them. In light of the severe disasters in the provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang, he has made a grand vow to donate all proceeds from his calligraphy commissions over three months to disaster relief. Couplets and hanging scrolls will be reduced by one yuan per piece, while four-panel screens will be doubled. True script, cursive script, clerical script, and seal script are all accepted, and he also prepares longevity couplets, celebratory couplets, elegiac couplets, longevity poems, eulogies, and portrait inscriptions. Each piece costs two yuan. Prices for longevity screens and epitaphs are also greatly reduced. Urgent orders can be collected the day after tomorrow, and small pieces can be completed immediately. Fellow artists who wish to exchange paintings for calligraphy are also welcome. Please address correspondence to the Yàdōng Bank on Tianjin Road, Shanghai.

Rickshaw Puller Hangs Himself; Rickshaw Pullers' Mutual Aid Association Investigates the Truth 153

The Shanghai Rickshaw Pullers' Mutual Aid Association, upon learning of the news report that a public rickshaw puller named Liú Diànyuán committed suicide due to a failed registration, dispatched investigators to ascertain the truth in order to provide relief to his family. It was learned that the rickshaw puller had previously pulled a public rickshaw for Zhāng Lìjì's rickshaw company three years ago. In the last three years, he had switched to pulling a private rickshaw for Mr. Sòng Wénxiáng, an employee of Tài Yǐ Malt Extract Company. On January 16 of this year, he applied for a private rickshaw registration at the Municipal Council Rickshaw Committee, application number 17364, registered under the name Liú Ā'èr (i.e., Dìyuán or Diànyuán). He went to the Xīnzha Road registration office, but due to poor eyesight, the registration office instructed him to return for a re-examination a week later. However, the next day (January 17), Liú instructed his brother-in-law, Wáng Zhèngxīng (also known as Āfú), to go to the Municipal Council Rickshaw Committee to collect private rickshaw application number 17384 and register it. He himself did not go for the re-examination. Recently, Liú Diànyuán, due to excessive debts accumulated over time and unable to cope, conceived a pessimistic thought and hanged himself in the middle of the night on April 1. After the Mutual Aid Association investigated the truth, it was determined that he was a private rickshaw puller and not a public rickshaw puller, and therefore not entitled to the Association's relief benefits.

Sawyers' Guild Reorganizes Regulations 155

The Sawyers' Guild of the Municipal Timber Workers' Union has had regulations in place for some time, but due to years of neglect, the order has become chaotic. If they are not reorganized, how can the welfare of the workers be improved and the industry's vitality be maintained? Yesterday, Táo Màolín, Lù Sēnguì, and others convened a meeting attended by over seventy people. Xú Chūnfā was elected as temporary chairman, and the meeting proceeded according to protocol. The chairman reported on the purpose of the meeting, and then discussions began: (1) It was proposed that the previous resolution regarding carpenters and sawyers working on projects undertaken by subcontractors, which was deemed a deliberate violation of industry regulations by construction contractors, should be penalized to prevent imitation. A letter had already been sent to the Construction Contractors' Association, but more than a month had passed without a response. The resolution to urge the Association again, and to send a formal letter of demand; (2) It was proposed to clearly delineate the boundaries between large saw and small saw departments. Resolution: A deadline should be set for all members to register and obtain professional certificates to avoid confusion; (3) It was proposed to establish a consumer cooperative. Resolution: The accounting department should plan and implement the proposal. The meeting adjourned after the discussions.

Industrial Accident Report for Last Month 156

According to reports received by the Municipal Council, although many factories experienced shutdowns and reduced production last month, there were still as many as 194 accidents, with six fatalities due to injuries. The causes of the accidents were largely understood in 154 cases, and 91 cases were investigated.

In terms of occupational breakdown, there were 56 accidents in the machinery and metal industry, with no fatalities, but many electrical injuries. There were 20 accidents in the textile industry, with one fatality. There were 16 accidents in the clothing industry, with one fatality. There were 16 accidents in the chemical industry. There were 4 accidents in public utilities, with one fatality. There were 13 accidents in the transportation industry, with one fatality. In terms of causal breakdown, 60 accidents were due to machinery, including 17 related to belts and gears and 18 related to presses. In addition, 31 accidents were caused by falling objects, and 25 accidents were caused by falls, with two fatalities.

Worker fatigue due to long hours was one of the causes of accidents. One worker, who had been in the factory since 6:00 PM, tripped over a machine part at 6:00 AM the next morning, resulting in a bone fracture. Another fourteen-year-old female worker, working until 2:00 AM, sat on a motor out of exhaustion. When the foreman called her, she mistakenly inserted her fingertip into the machine casing, causing it to be crushed.

The lack of protective devices on machinery makes it easy for clothing, sleeves, and hair to be caught and cause injury. Several factories have already begun protective work.

Selected Poems of Tang Monks Published: Selected by Layman Pí Hèlíng, this book specializes in collecting poems written by Buddhist monks and chan practitioners of the Tang Dynasty, during their moments of inspiration outside of chanting, which are either like the roar of a dragon, the roar of a tiger, the cry of a wild crane in the sky, or the echo of a secluded spring. Each song and poem flows from the light of the heart, without artifice, naturally simple and lofty, and everywhere searches for its beauty. Unfortunately, selectors in the past have often valued Confucianism over Buddhism, and there have been few special selections of monk poems for later generations to appreciate. The compilation of this book is enough to fill this gap. In total, the book contains over 551 poems by more than 50 authors, all of which are the artistic essence of the Tang Dynasty. The entire book is priced at 4 jiao and distributed by the Buddhist Bookstore on Jiāozhōu Road, Shanghai, and its branches in various locations.

Sports News

First Standing Committee Meeting of the National Games Organizing Committee: Nomination of Section Chiefs, Approval of Competition and Judging Committee Organizational Rules, etc. The Organizing Committee Office will be located at the City Center Sports Field, starting operations on the 22nd of this month. 163

The Preparatory Committee for the Sixth National Games held its first standing committee meeting at the City Government Conference Room yesterday morning at 9:30 AM. The meeting nominated candidates for section chief positions in each group, approved the procedural rules for the organizing committee, and the organizational rules for both the judging and competition committees. It was also decided that the office would begin operations at the City Center Sports Field starting on the 22nd of this month. Details are as follows:

Attendees of the Standing Committee Meeting: Standing Committee members Wu Tiecheng, Pan Gongzhan, Hao Gengsheng, Wang Shijie (representing Hao), Lei Zhen (representing Hao), Cai Zengji, Cai Jinjun, Shen Siliang, Xu Peihuang, Chu Minyi (representing Shao Rugan). Also in attendance were Deputy Secretaries-General Jiang Xiangqing, Shao Rugan, Ma Chonggan. The meeting was chaired by Mayor Wu, and recorded by Wang Youxu of the City Education Bureau.

Nomination of Section Chiefs: After formal greetings, the following items were discussed: (1) Nomination of section chiefs in each group, as discussed in the first preparatory meeting. Resolution: The following nominations for section chiefs of the Sixth National Games Preparatory Committee were approved: Ma Chonggan, concurrently head of the Documentation Section; Shen Siliang, concurrently head of the General Affairs Section; Representative from the City Bank, head of the Accounting Section; Chen Kecheng, head of the Publicity Section; Chen Xiangtao, head of the Reception Section; Representative from the Public Security Bureau, head of the Security Section; Representative from the Public Works Bureau, head of the Transportation Section; Representative from the Health Bureau, head of the Health Section; Zhou Jiaqi, head of the Venue Equipment Section; Wu Bangwei, head of the Registration and Allocation Subsection; Jiang Xiangqing, concurrently head of the Judging Subsection; Chen Kuisheng, concurrently head of the Records Subsection; Shao Rugan, concurrently head of the Awards Subsection; Xu Zhiyi, head of the National Arts Subsection.

Discussion of Submitted Cases: (2) The procedural rules for the Preparatory Committee, as discussed in the first preparatory meeting. Resolution: Approved. (3) The competition regulations for the Sixth National Games, as discussed in the first preparatory meeting. Resolution: Except for Articles 15, section 5, and Article 29, which were referred to the Secretary-General, Deputy Secretary-General, and Standing Committee member Hao Gengsheng for review and amendment to be discussed at the next Standing Committee meeting, all other articles were approved as is. (4) The organizational rules for the Competition Committee of the Sixth National Games, as discussed in the first preparatory meeting. Resolution: Approved with amendments. (5) The organizational rules for the Judging Committee of the Sixth National Games, as discussed in the first preparatory meeting. Resolution: Approved with amendments. (6) Review of the competition rulebooks for various sports events of the Games, as discussed in the first preparatory meeting. Resolution: To be reviewed by Standing Committee member Hao Gengsheng in conjunction with the Secretary-General and Deputy Secretary-General and submitted for discussion at the next Standing Committee meeting. (7) How to proceed with the work plans of each group, as discussed in the first preparatory meeting. Resolution: Each section to draft a plan and submit it for discussion at the next Standing Committee meeting. (8) Proposed performance items for the Games, as discussed in the first preparatory meeting. Resolution: To be handled by the Registration and Allocation Subsection. (9) The method of calculating the overall championship points for the Games, as discussed in the first preparatory meeting. Resolution: To be reviewed jointly by the Secretary-General, Deputy Secretary-General, and Standing Committee member Hao and submitted for discussion at the next Standing Committee meeting.

Date Set for Commencement of Operations: (10) The location of the office and the date of commencement of operations. Resolution: The City Center Sports Field was designated as the location for the office, and operations will commence on April 22nd (Monday). (11) The issuance of an official seal for use. Resolution: To be designed by the committee and reported to the ministry upon use. The meeting adjourned at 11 AM.

Procedural Rules for the Organizing Committee: The Procedural Rules for the Preparatory Committee of the Sixth National Games. Article 1: These rules are established in accordance with Article 19 of the Organizational Regulations of the Preparatory Committee of the Sixth National Games. All staff members of the committee shall conduct their work in accordance with these rules. Article 2: Staff members of the committee shall sign in and work at the office during the designated hours. If necessary, these hours may be extended or started earlier. (From 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM, and from 1:00 PM to 5:00 PM). Article 3: Staff members of the committee who need to take leave must find a replacement to perform their duties. Article 4: The minutes of the committee meetings and the meetings of the executive directors shall be handled by the Documentation Section. The minutes of meetings of each section shall be handled by the respective sections themselves. Article 5: Regulations and guidelines drafted by each section must be submitted to the Documentation Section and then submitted to the committee for approval before they can take effect. Article 6: Any news releases from each section that need to be published externally must be submitted to the Publicity Section for publication in the committee's daily bulletin or in various newspapers. Article 7: If each section intends to purchase equipment, the head of the section must prepare a purchase list, including the name, quantity, price, and purpose of the items, and submit it to the Secretary-General or Deputy Secretary-General for approval before the purchase can be made. Article 8: When each section needs to use funds for official business, the person in charge must sign and affix their seal, and the head of the section must approve it. After review by the auditor, it must be approved by the Secretary-General or Deputy Secretary-General before it can be withdrawn. Article 9: When each section needs to use items, they must fill out a requisition form, which must be approved by the head of the section, and then obtain the items from the General Affairs Section. However, all items used, except for consumables, must be returned after use. Article 10: All incoming and outgoing documents or requests for files of the committee must be stamped with a seal. Article 11: No visitors are allowed in the committee office. Article 12: The operating guidelines for each section shall be established separately. Article 13: If these rules are incomplete, they may be amended at any time after being proposed by the committee and approved at a meeting. Article 14: These rules shall be implemented after being resolved and approved by the Preparatory Committee.

Organizational Rules for the Competition Committee: The Organizational Rules for the Competition Committee of the Sixth National Games. Article 1: This committee (hereinafter referred to as "the Committee") is organized by the Preparatory Committee, in accordance with Articles 9 and 10 of the Organizational Regulations of the Preparatory Committee of the Sixth National Games, and consists of 15 to 19 members appointed by the Preparatory Committee. It is responsible for all competition matters. Article 2: The Committee is the highest authority for competition affairs in the Games. In accordance with Article 11 of the Preparatory Committee's regulations, a chairman shall be appointed, who shall be mutually elected by the members of the Competition Committee. The chairman shall implement all resolutions of the Committee and be responsible for convening meetings. Article 3: The Committee is divided into the following sections in accordance with the Organizational Regulations of the Preparatory Committee: (1) Venue Equipment Section; (2) Registration and Allocation Section; (3) Judging Section; (4) Records Section; (5) Awards Section; (6) National Arts Section. Article 4: Each section of the Committee shall have one section chief and several staff members. Depending on the complexity of the section's affairs, assistant staff members and clerks may be hired to handle the affairs of each section. Article 5: In addition to the responsibilities stipulated by the Organizational Regulations of the Preparatory Committee, each section shall also formulate its own work plan. Article 6: While in charge of their respective affairs, each section shall also act upon the orders of the Preparatory Committee Chairman and the Secretary-General of the Games. Article 7: The Committee shall hold a regular meeting every two weeks. Special meetings may be held when necessary. Article 8: Each section's business meeting shall be held once a week. Special meetings may be held when necessary. Article 9: The Procedural Rules of the Preparatory Committee shall apply to the Committee's operational rules. Article 10: These regulations shall be implemented after being resolved and approved by the Preparatory Committee of the Sixth National Games.

Organizational Rules for the Judging Committee: The Organizational Rules for the Judging Committee of the Sixth National Games. Article 1: This committee (hereinafter referred to as "the Committee") is organized by the Preparatory Committee, in accordance with Articles 9 and 11 of the Organizational Regulations of the Preparatory Committee of the Sixth National Games, and consists of 15 to 19 members appointed by the Preparatory Committee. It is responsible for all judging matters. Article 2: The Committee is the highest judging authority for the Games. In accordance with Article 14 of the Preparatory Committee's regulations, a chairman shall be appointed, who shall be mutually elected by the members of the Judging Committee. The chairman shall be responsible for all affairs of the Committee and for convening meetings of the Committee. Article 3: The responsibilities of the Committee are as follows: (1) To review and approve competition rules and regulations; (2) To review, approve, and interpret the rules for various sports events; (3) To review the qualifications of athletes; (4) To reward or punish the conduct of athletes; (5) To adjudicate competition disputes; (6) To supervise the order of various sports venues. Article 4: The Committee shall not hold regularly scheduled meetings. The chairman shall convene meetings at a time determined by the importance of the matter. Article 5: The rules for the Committee's judging meetings shall be established separately. Article 6: The Procedural Rules of the Preparatory Committee shall apply to the Committee's operational rules. Article 7: These regulations shall be implemented after being resolved and approved by the Preparatory Committee of the Sixth National Games.
