Education News

Legislative Yuan Meeting Passes Degree Conferral Law 172

(Central News Agency, Nanjing, 12th) The Legislative Yuan held its 12th meeting on the morning of the 12th. 69 members, including Dai Xiujun, were present, with Sun Ke presiding and Liang Hancao as Secretary-General. The only item discussed was the "Degree Conferral Law," which was resolved to be passed with amendments according to the review report of the Legal System Committee. The draft Degree Regulations was resolved by the Yuan meeting on May 18, 1929 to be reviewed by members such as Dai Xiujun. Subsequently, at the Yuan meeting on July 16 of the same year, according to the review report of member Dai and others, it was submitted for discussion and resolved to be sent back to the original review committee for review. At the Yuan meeting on July 12, 1930, member Dai and others submitted the re-reviewed case and attached implementing regulations for review. The Yuan meeting then resolved to proceed with the review. At the Yuan meeting on November 8 of the same year, based on the proposal of Wei Tingsheng, the case was again submitted to the original review committee, along with members Jiao Yitang and Luo Ding, for review. By the time of the Yuan meeting on December 4 of the same year, member Dai and others submitted the re-reviewed case, changing the "Degree Conferral Law" to "Doctoral Degree Conferral Law," to the meeting. The Yuan then resolved to proceed with the review. In May 1933, the National Government sent a letter urging the speedy formulation of degree regulations, so it was again submitted to the Legal System Committee for review. Subsequently, the National Government issued the "Principles of the Degree Conferral Law" and the "Draft of the Degree Conferral Law" to the Yuan, which were submitted to the committee for review together. Now, the review has finally been completed and submitted to the meeting for passage. The case has lasted for six years, and can be said to be a difficult birth. At today's meeting, when deliberating on this case, Xi Chaojun and Dai Xiujun first reported on the review process separately. Then, the second reading began. Except for some debate among the members on Article 6, which stipulates that those with special contributions to scholarship may also be candidates for a doctoral degree, there were no other objections. Zhou Wei, Luo Yunyan, and others argued that the scope of the article, which stipulates that those with special writings or inventions in scholarship and those who have served as professors at universities or independent colleges for more than three years are eligible to be candidates for a doctoral degree, was too broad and could lead to abuse and harm the reputation of the nation. Cheng Zhonghang, Zhong Tianxin, Di Ying, and others argued that the provision was intended to encourage those with special contributions to scholarship, and that the current university organization law strictly limits the qualifications of professors, so there would be no abuse of the nation's reputation. Therefore, they firmly advocated maintaining the original proposal. The chairman then put it to a vote. Only five people supported the proposal of Zhou and Luo. As a result, the original proposal was passed. The meeting adjourned at 11 AM.

Articles of the Degree Conferral Law 173

The twelve articles of the Degree Conferral Law are as follows: Article 1: The conferral of degrees shall be in accordance with the provisions of this law. Article 2: Degrees are divided into three levels: Bachelor's, Master's, and Doctoral. However, special disciplines may only have two levels or one level. The detailed regulations for the aforementioned levels shall be determined by the Ministry of Education. Article 3: Those who have completed their studies at a public or registered private university or independent college, passed the examinations, and have been verified by the Ministry of Education without objection shall be awarded a Bachelor's degree by the university or independent college. Article 4: Those who have received a Bachelor's degree in accordance with this law and have continued their studies for more than two years at a graduate school or research institute of a public or registered private university or independent college, and have been assessed by the graduate school or research institute as having satisfactory results, may be nominated by the graduate school or research institute as candidates for a Master's degree. Master's degree candidates who pass the examinations and have been verified by the Ministry of Education without objection shall be awarded a Master's degree by the university or independent college. The detailed regulations for the Master's degree examinations shall be determined by the Ministry of Education. Article 5: Those who have received a Master's degree in accordance with this law and have continued their studies for more than two years at the graduate school or research institute stipulated in the preceding article, and have been assessed by the graduate school or research institute as having satisfactory results and have been approved by the Ministry of Education, may be candidates for a Doctoral degree. Article 6: Those who possess one of the following qualifications and have been assessed as qualified by the Ministry of Education may also be candidates for a Doctoral degree: (1) Those who have special writings or inventions in scholarship; (2) Those who have served as professors at public or registered private universities or independent colleges for more than three years. Article 7: Doctoral degree candidates who pass the examinations of the Doctoral Degree Evaluation Committee shall be awarded a Doctoral degree by the state. The organization of the Doctoral Degree Evaluation Committee and the detailed regulations for the Doctoral degree examinations shall be determined by the Executive Yuan in conjunction with the Examination Yuan. Article 8: Candidates for Master's and Doctoral degrees must submit a research thesis. Article 9: Graduates of undergraduate programs at public or registered private universities or independent colleges before the implementation of this law and those who have received a Bachelor's degree in accordance with Article 3 shall have the same qualifications. Article 10: Those who have obtained degrees from foreign schools or other academic institutions recognized by the Ministry of Education may use the title of a certain degree from a certain school in a certain country. Article 11: The conferral of honorary Doctoral degrees shall be determined by a separate law. Article 12: The date of implementation of this law shall be determined by order.

Fifth Day of Reading Campaign: Tao Baichuan on How to Study Party Principles; Li Ximou to Lecture on How to Study Natural Science at Zhongxi Radio at 3:15 PM Today 176

Yesterday was the fifth day of the National Reading Campaign, organized by the Chinese Cultural Reconstruction Association. The association specially invited Tao Baichuan to lecture on how to study Party Principles at Zhongxi Radio. Today, from 3:15 PM to 3:45 PM, the association has invited Li Ximou, Dean of the Science College of National Jinan University, to lecture on how to study natural science at Zhongxi Radio. The full text of Tao Baichuan's lecture is recorded below:

Superficial Research. Ladies and gentlemen, today the Chinese Cultural Reconstruction Association invited me to lecture on how to study Party Principles. The so-called Party Principles, of course, refer to the Three Principles of the People of the Chinese Kuomintang. So, how to study Party Principles is how to study the Three Principles of the People of the Chinese Kuomintang. There are two ways to study the Three Principles of the People of the Chinese Kuomintang: one is superficial research, and the other is in-depth research. Now, let's talk about the method of superficial research. The so-called origin of the Three Principles of the People is the draft of Sun Yat-sen's speeches at Guangzhou University in the twelfth year of the Republic of China, including the three aspects of nationalism, democracy, and people's livelihood. There are six lectures on nationalism, six lectures on democracy, and four lectures on people's livelihood. These sixteen lectures contain the essence of the entire theory of the Three Principles of the People. This is a must-read book for studying the Three Principles of the People. However, a complete doctrine must include two parts: one is the theoretical system, and the other is the method of practice. A doctrine is not complete if it only has a method of practice without profound theories, or if it only has profound theories without a method of practice. The Three Principles of the People has its profound theories and, of course, its methods of practice.

Methods of Practice. The method of practice of the Three Principles of the People is the National Reconstruction Program, which includes three parts. The first is Sun Wen's Doctrine, which is psychological reconstruction. Mr. Sun Yat-sen, in view of the fact that people generally suffer too deeply from the poison of "knowing is difficult, acting is easy," believed that the reason why China had failed in everything for thousands of years was entirely due to the poison of "knowing is difficult, acting is easy." Therefore, he advocated knowing is easy, acting is difficult, to correct the erroneous psychology of the Chinese people for thousands of years. He provided many pieces of evidence and explained many principles to prove the correctness of knowing is easy, acting is difficult. The second is the Industrial Plan. Given China's vast land and abundant resources, with wealth hidden in the earth, yet the people suffer hardship and lack means of livelihood, he provided detailed plans for China's agriculture, industry, commerce, transportation, and the people's clothing, food, housing, and transportation in the Industrial Plan, completing a great industrial plan. The third is the Fundamentals of Democracy. China claims to have 470 million people, yet they are like a heap of loose sand, without unity. They only sweep the snow from their own doors and do not care about the frost on other people's roofs. There is no concept of unity at all, and group life is, of course, out of the question. Therefore, in the Fundamentals of Democracy, Mr. Sun stipulated the methods of assembly and association, the order of meetings and discussions, and so on. Therefore, "Sun Wen's Doctrine" is to transform the people's psychology, the "Industrial Plan" is to build the nation's economy, and the "Fundamentals of Democracy" is to guide the people in cooperation and collaboration. In addition to the National Reconstruction Program, there is also the Outline of National Reconstruction. Although this book has only 25 articles, it details the goals of national reconstruction, the procedures of national reconstruction, and how to solve the problems between nationalism, democracy, and people's livelihood. It also specifies how to implement the three stages of military government, tutelage government, and constitutional government. In just a few hundred words, it provides a complete outline and summary for us. It can be said that the Outline of National Reconstruction is entirely based on the Three Principles of the People and the National Reconstruction Program, and it is a complete national construction plan. In addition to the above two books, there is also the Method for Implementing Local Self-Government. In this book, Mr. Sun gave a concise explanation of the importance of local self-government and the methods of its implementation. It must be known that local self-government is the fundamental work of national construction. If local self-government cannot be completed, other constructions are out of the question. The saying "cultivate oneself, regulate one's family, govern the country, and pacify the world" means that everything should be approached with a broad perspective and start from small things. Local self-government is the foundation of a country, so we cannot neglect this book. To study the theory of the Three Principles of the People, one must read Mr. Sun's lectures on the Three Principles of the People carefully. To study the methods of the Three Principles of the People, one must read the National Reconstruction Program, the Outline of National Reconstruction, and the Method for Implementing Local Self-Government.

Philosophical Research. The above is the method of superficial research, and now I will talk about the method of in-depth research. There are three methods of in-depth research: first, research from a philosophical perspective; second, research from a historical perspective; and third, comparative research. The so-called research from a philosophical perspective is to study the ontology of the Three Principles of the People. A complete doctrine must have a method of observing the past, a plan for transforming the present, and an ideal goal for the future. Mr. Sun Yat-sen believed that there was a fundamental force dominating and driving everything in the history of the past and the evolution of all societies. From a historical perspective, we can see that the evolution from hunting and gathering societies to nomadic societies, from nomadic societies to agricultural societies, and then to industrial societies, from barbarism to civilization, is all driven by a great force, which is people's livelihood. To study the Three Principles of the People from a philosophical perspective, one must study Mr. Sun's view of history based on people's livelihood, which is the historical view of vitality. There are two major schools of philosophy: idealism and materialism. Mr. Sun's philosophical foundation is neither idealism nor materialism, but vitality. As for the detailed explanation of vitality, how it differs from idealism and materialism, and why it is superior to materialism and idealism, I will discuss it later due to time constraints today.

Research from the Perspective of the Times. The second method of research is to focus on the perspective of the times, that is, to research from a historical perspective. It is important to know that every doctrine has its historical background, and it is by no means the fantasy of scholars at their desks or in their studies. Only when national problems arise does nationalism emerge. Only when democratic problems arise does democracy emerge. If China today had no problems of nationalism, democracy, and people's livelihood, Mr. Sun would never have advocated the Three Principles of the People. Because the Three Principles of the People meet the needs of the times, the doctrine itself is entirely aimed at the needs of the national conditions and the trend of the world. Various policies and programs based on the doctrine are, of course, established in response to the requirements of a certain time and environment, and can also change with changes in a certain time and environment. This is the second method of researching the Three Principles of the People from a historical perspective.

Comparative Research. The third method of researching the Three Principles of the People is to start from a comparative perspective. Today, at the same time and in the same space, many doctrines are presented before us, including nationalism, communism, anarchism, cosmopolitanism, and socialism. Their theories are different, and their methods are different. How can we believe in the Three Principles of the People and not believe in other doctrines? Why are other doctrines not suitable for China, while only the Three Principles of the People is suitable? To have a deep understanding of these issues, we must conduct in-depth research. Only then can our faith be firm, and our revolutionary path can be firmly grasped. For example, a comparison between nationalism and state-ism, a comparison between nationalism and cosmopolitanism, a comparison between democracy and anarchism, a comparison between democracy and democracy, a comparison between the principle of people's livelihood and capitalism, and a comparison between the principle of people's livelihood and communism are all worth studying in depth in order to arrive at correct conclusions and establish our correct faith.

Introduction to Research Books. The methods of studying the Three Principles of the People have been briefly described above. Now, I will introduce several research books to you. Mr. Sun's Three Principles of the People, National Reconstruction Program, Outline of National Reconstruction, and Method for Implementing Local Self-Government are, of course, must-reads. I will now introduce some reference books to you. For superficial research, there is my Three Principles of the People: An Overview and Mr. Zhou Fohai's The Theoretical System of the Three Principles of the People. For in-depth research, Chen Lifu's The Vitalism can be used for philosophical research, and the world history and national history of the past century must be consulted for research from the perspective of the times. Hu Hanmin's The Operational Nature of the Three Principles of the People is also a reference book that we must read. That is all.

Review and Expectations of the Publishing World 180

— Ye Qing

Culture is very important in modern life. Comparing our culture with that of Europe and the United States, we are very backward. Therefore, there is an urgent need for effort. This is well known and does not need to be said.

Those engaged in cultural activities include education, academic organizations, etc., but the publishing industry is particularly important. All cultural activities, whether related to thinking or practice, whether related to improvement or popularization, can be seen in the publishing industry. Therefore, to understand our cultural situation, we must review the publishing industry.

Our publishing industry has a considerable range. Government, schools, social groups, bookstores, and individuals are all participating. Needless to say, among these participants, bookstores are specialized and at the center.

But regardless of whether you speak specifically from the perspective of bookstores or generally, our publishing industry has various shortcomings, which are very obvious. Benefits? There seems to be nothing. And it doesn't matter if we don't talk about it. The important thing is to point out the shortcomings and find a direction for effort to promote our activities.

In this way, I will begin to analyze the shortcomings of the publishing industry.

In terms of quantity, compared with countries such as Japan, the United States, the United Kingdom, France, Germany, and Italy, the things we publish in a year are far behind. According to Mr. Shu Xincheng's estimate, last year, "the total for the whole year was about 2,160 volumes, 1,716 types, which, compared with the number of publications in various countries in the world in 1931, was only more than Switzerland and ranked 16th. If compared by population, each new publication only accounts for 219,230 people, which is indeed less than any other country." (Cultural Construction, Volume 1, Issue 3, Page 105) Can such a small situation still be called a civilized country?

In terms of quality, there are very few philosophical and scientific works, and profound ones are even rarer. Relatively speaking, there is a little more literature. And the most is the reprinting of ancient books. Some bookstores publish them repeatedly, such as the Twenty-Four Histories, the Twenty-Five Histories, and the Twenty-Six Histories. In addition, they compete to publish textbooks for various levels of schools. Children's books have also become a trend in publishing activities in recent years. Needless to say, pictorials are particularly developed.

From the perspective of both the quantity and quality of publications, it can be said that the current direction of efforts should be these points:

First, increase the quantity;

Second, publish more books on philosophy and science;

Third, pay attention to advanced works.

This is naturally related to China's needs. And there are also reasons for the poverty of past publications in terms of both quantity and quality. Taken together, it is the underdeveloped production, the bankruptcy of the countryside, and an era of overall economic recession, undeveloped education, and the lack of a research atmosphere. There are too many teachers, students, and ordinary people who do not read books and do not buy books. In this situation, it is impossible for publications not to be poor. (To be continued)

My Reading Experience 181

— Wang Xinming

According to my personal reading experience, it seems that there are three methods of reading: first, diligent reading; second, thorough reading; and third, careful reading.

Now let's talk about diligent reading first. "Proficiency comes from diligence, and idleness leads to waste." This is an unchangeable conclusion throughout the ages. Therefore, no matter what books you read, diligent reading is always the first priority. But what I mean by diligent reading here is not advocating a prison-like reading life. It means that you should pay attention to active reading during the reading time; as long as you can concentrate, don't think about "the arrival of the swan," and don't let external affairs disturb your reading and divide your reading time. This is considered diligent reading. I have considerable experience in this regard. Before I was fourteen years old, I didn't understand the benefits of diligent reading. I always liked to play with flowers, trees, insects, and birds. I was in the study room, but my heart was outside the room. I was reciting books, but my heart was remembering the budding roses, the sprouting willows, the ant nests by the wall, and the magpie nests in the trees. As a result, the books I had read were equal to not reading. When I was fourteen years old, I was stimulated by the diligent reading of my classmates and realized that I could not grasp the essentials of the book or make any achievements without diligent reading. So, I changed my attitude of reading while indulging my imagination in external objects; during the reading time, I made full use of this time to read; when it was not reading time, I made full use of this free time to play. This resulted in very good results. Because I was originally the youngest and most academically immature among more than 30 classmates, and my grades were always the lowest in each exam. After diligent reading, my knowledge quickly caught up with my classmates, and by the end of the year, I was able to compete with the oldest and most knowledgeable classmates for first place.

It is not enough to be diligent in reading; in addition to diligence, you must also be thorough. What is thorough reading? "Learning and practicing it from time to time" is thorough reading. Although "learning and practicing it from time to time" is only reviewing the old, if you don't review the old, you can't know the new. Therefore, reviewing the old has great significance in reading. When I was young, when I heard the saying of reviewing the old and knowing the new, I always thought it was meaningless. Later, as I grew older and my memory declined, when I flipped through the books I had read but not thoroughly, they all looked like unfamiliar faces. Only then did I realize that I must read books thoroughly to be able to remember them for a long time. If I let them go lightly, it would be equivalent to not reading them.

Diligent reading and thorough reading are certainly very important, but careful reading is also very important. Careful reading has two meanings. First, it means choosing the books that must be read and not seeking breadth or quantity. Second, it means not letting go of the key points in the book, so that the books you have read are not read in vain. Why? Because seeking breadth and quantity will make the mistake of "coveting more and getting less." The more you want to be a person who knows all books, the more you will end up not knowing any book. Instead of boasting about breadth and quantity, and not being able to read a book carefully, it is better to carefully select the essence of the books to read and ensure that useful time is not wasted on indiscriminate reading. I remember when I was twenty-one or two years old, I liked to read poetry indiscriminately. I always thought that the more I read, the better my own poetry would be. Unexpectedly, the result was that the more I read, the more my own poetry became patchwork. Later, after I suddenly realized this, I spent more than a year studying Tang poetry carefully and without distraction, and I got unexpected gains. The poems signed "Wandering King" are now actually honored to be circulated for a while, which is the result of more than a year of careful study of Tang poetry without distraction.

In short, in the matter of reading, you must combine the three methods of diligence, thoroughness, and care to achieve considerable results. If you don't use these three methods to read, the effect will certainly not be great. The reason why people in the past sighed with "exhausting the classics with white hair" is that they only knew diligent reading and thorough reading, but did not know careful reading. Since the result of not knowing careful reading is that you will be unsuccessful even with white hair, then we should know to draw inferences from one instance and think of the result of only knowing careful reading but not knowing diligent reading and thorough reading.

Zhou Zuoren's "Origins of New Chinese Literature" 182

— Wang Fuquan

Published by the Renwen Bookstore in Beiping, Actual Price Five Jiao

Mr. Zhou Zuoren's "Origins of New Chinese Literature" is an important work in recent years. Of course, Mr. Zhou's literary views represent a part of the scholars; and I think the importance of this work does not lie in this, but in the advocacy of "belles-lettres". The high-profile Gong'an School and Jingling School and their advocates are in this book; the one that makes a promotional introduction to Shen Qitian's "A Selection of Modern Prose" is this book ("A Selection of Modern Prose" was previously named "Ice and Snow Sketches" and was selected by Ba'er, see "Camel Leather"). Of course, the popularity of "belles-lettres" has its own social basis, and even "humorous sketches" (belles-lettres are not necessarily humorous in content, this refers to those whose writing is belles-lettres and whose content is humorous) and even "sly and glib sketches" have their own social basis; and in seeking it on paper, we cannot but trace it back to this work. Yuan Zhonglang, the dead literary style of the Sixteen Masters of the Late Ming Dynasty is popular for a generation - no, fashionable for a while (judging from sales, it is not popular for a generation), all credit and blame must be attributed to this work.

We can say that Mr. Zhou's literary views, from "Literature of People" (this article appeared in "New Youth" and was an important essay at the time, but not many people noticed it) to this work, are consistently the same. Let's not talk about historical issues; Mr. Zhou advocates the literature of "expressing aspirations" (Mr. Zhou opposed "expressing aspirations" to "conveying the Way"). The social basis of the literature of "expressing aspirations" (as Mr. Zhou said) is very clear, which is the so-called "capitalism" and the products of capitalism. Mr. Zhou advocates the literature of "expressing aspirations" based on his consistent spirit since the May Fourth Movement, which is completely correct; then, is not the "humanitarianism" in the "Literature of People," that "humanitarianism," "the Way"? No, no, that is precisely the "aspiration" of the May Fourth era.

Introducing Bacon's "New Organon" 183

— Du Ruoyi

Published by Xinken Bookstore, Translated by Shen Yinming

Since the May Fourth Movement, Chinese scholars have been very active in introducing Western culture, but very few of the important works of any field of learning have been translated in their original form. Marx has been introduced for many years and has had a great influence in the ideological world, but "Das Kapital" has not been fully translated to this day. Writers have been talking about Tolstoy, but there is no translation of Tolstoy's great works. Philosophers always talk about Bacon and Kant, but where are the translations of Bacon and Kant's philosophical works? Therefore, the method of introduction by Chinese scholars really makes people feel like grasping at shadows.

The most important thing in the Chinese cultural world today is to show the existing achievements of Chinese and Western cultures to cultural people with genuine goods. What is Confucius's theory? Should it be inherited? Should it be abandoned? What is Marxism? Should it be supported? Should it be opposed? There must always be genuine goods to see, and only after seeing them can decisions be made. Scholars must study monographs when they seek knowledge. It is not enough to simply read some magazines and articles that introduce the superficial aspects. But first of all, there must be monographs to read. Not all scholars know foreign languages, and those who know foreign languages do not necessarily know everything. Therefore, various monographs must have translations. Whoever can translate an important academic masterpiece is a meritorious person in the Chinese cultural world today.

Now I see that Bacon's famous work, "Novum Organum," has a translation, and I am very happy and want to introduce it here.

Francis Bacon was a great British philosopher, proficient in law and economics, and also an astronomer. He was born in London in 1561. At the age of thirteen, he entered Trinity College, Cambridge. He left the college three years later. In 1582, he became a lawyer. In 1616, he was elected as a member of Parliament. Later, he served as Royal Counsel and Attorney General. In 1618, he became Lord Chancellor at the age of 57. In 1621, he was arrested and imprisoned for bribery. He was pardoned by the King a few days later and devoted himself to research and writing. He died in 1626. He opposed Aristotle's doctrines and wanted to rescue philosophy from the tedious disputes of scholasticism. He advocated directly experiencing nature and taking inductive methods based on observation and experience as the true method of understanding nature. His theories had a great influence on modern science, so he is known as the "father of modern science." His works include Essays, The Advancement of Learning, and New Organon. (To be continued)

If this request can be granted by various publishers, then the book and newspaper reports of this magazine may not be difficult to provide better service to readers in the future.

The Hobby of Reading 185

— Xie Liuyi

I once read a poem by Francis. Beulloch, the content of which was about reading. The general idea is:

I love books as a drunkard loves wine,

The more I drink, the more I feel the spirit within,

My soul rejoices and is immersed in love,

Raising my glass again, I find the taste inexhaustible.

Wherever I am, books are my companions,

Bringing comfort in times of loneliness,

And friendship in times of solitude.

Books! My treasures,

You are my dearest friends.

Your value is pure,

Your friendship sincere.

Because of you, I can whisper with the sages of the past,

And be close to the talented people of today.

Within, I see much joy and sorrow,

Those joys and sorrows touch my heart.

After reading the original poem, I translated it and wrote it in one of my favorite books. The sentiment of the poem is good, but I do not quite agree with the analogy of the hobby of reading to the attitude of a drunkard towards drinking.

Although those who drink know that alcohol can numb human nature, drunkards still love to drink, not stopping until they are "dead drunk." If readers were to adopt the attitude of a drunkard, I think it would be unsuitable. Reading a lot is certainly good, but one must not read until one is dazed, like being drunk. The best way to drink is to be "slightly tipsy" without getting completely drunk; the best way to read is to become clearer-headed the more one reads, to be able to use the knowledge in the books actively, and not to be bound by the books. Being bound by books is the same as being numbed by alcohol, resulting in becoming a "fossil" of books.

What kind of books should one read? Apart from the books one specializes in, it is advisable to "meander" or "read widely." For example, a person who studies philosophy, in addition to books on philosophy, may wish to expand the scope of their reading to gardening, bird-keeping, etc., and discover knowledge related to philosophy from those books. Wouldn't that be interesting? (April 5th)

Chunqiu (Spring and Autumn)

Tidbits 198

— (Chen Yunsu)

Almost every young person likes to recall the past, yearn for the future, and curse the reality. Because the past is like a fruit of remonstrance, giving people a sweet aftertaste; the future is like a sugarcane, the more you eat, the sweeter it becomes, and the more flavorful it becomes later; only reality is worthy of being cursed, hated, not knowing how to grasp reality is to create happiness for the future and the best material for remembering the past.

When Sister Spring hasn't married us, we are despite suffering from unrequited love, and we think how lovely and how beautiful she is! When she marries us, we put her aside, never return to the embrace of nature, the green world, and caress her, and be affectionate with her. When her spring passes and her beauty fades, we immediately write about her and express her in words, to mourn her, and sigh for her. I don't know if it is Sister Spring who has failed us, or we have failed Sister Spring!

Talking About Touring the Lake 199

— Master Shiyuan

I have been staying in Kangyuan for three or four springs without realizing it. Although I dare not say that I am an old horse who knows the way for the "West Lake," which has been known for its beauty since ancient times, I am confident that I have a considerable understanding of it. Taking advantage of this time when the flowers are fragrant and tourists are woven, I will briefly, objectively, and concretely talk about the lake scenery, providing a reference for the ladies who are obsessed with the scenery of West Lake.

The Ten Scenes of West Lake are the central goals that everyone yearns for. In fact, these so-called ten scenes are mostly the mysteries that Emperor Qianlong made. There is a "Royal Monument" in each scene. Most of the ten scenes are abstract and empty. In other words, they do not escape the "poetic" and "fantasy" of Chinese literati, and they cannot come up with real evidence. In the "Willow Waves and Orioles" in the Ten Scenes, there are few willows, and even if there are, the orioles have nowhere to live. "Broken Bridge Remaining Snow" has now become a Kangzhuang Bridge, and cars pass without hindrance. "Su Causeway in the Spring Dawn", I don't know what it refers to? "Double Peaks Piercing the Clouds" must be viewed from a large area, but there are more than just double peaks that pierce the clouds. "Curved Courtyard with Lotus in the Breeze", the courtyard is very simple, and lotus flowers are occasionally decorated in summer. "Nanping Evening Bell". The emptiness can be seen from the noun. As for "Leifeng Pagoda in the Evening Glow", there is actually a reason, but unfortunately the tower collapsed ten years ago. It is almost always "Three Pools Mirroring the Moon" and "Autumn Moon over the Peaceful Lake". Every moonlit night, the scenery is indeed elegant. "Viewing Fish at Flower Harbor", you don't have to be fooled. The harbor is not a harbor, there are few flowers, and it is rare to have a few fish more than five inches long.

What I said above is not to spoil the fun, it is indeed the real situation. If you really play on the lake, some unknown places have a special flavor. There are also some relatively famous "caves", such as "Huanglong Cave", "Stone House Cave", "Jingu Cave", etc., which are very quiet and elegant and can be visited. Several "Zhuangzi" also have considerable meaning. In addition, the five-colored fish in "Yuquan" and the bamboo in "Yunxi" and "Taoguang" can all be played. The two "Tianzhus" and the "Jingci"... and other Buddhist temple places, the names are indeed deafening, but if you are not a Buddhist disciple, you don't have to go.

Country Wedding Feast 200

— Rongyu

In Shanghai, people who are popular? Receiving a wedding invitation from relatives and friends, they throw it on the table without nostalgia. People with more generous economies, beforehand, order the servants to send a generous gift; awkward friends, send it when they eat it. When the wedding day comes, those who have enough friendship, go to say congratulations in the morning; go to see the wedding in the afternoon, and enter the seat in the evening, and it is over after eating a full meal. Eating wedding wine in Shanghai, I really feel that it is a common and monotonous thing.

The situation in the countryside is very different. Not only are the people who have weddings killing pigs and chickens, and are busy; but also the people who eat wedding wine are also eating big fish and meat non-stop. Within a month before the event, they either rock the boat or pull up their pants, inviting relatives to the east and shouting neighbors to the west. Their invitation is a verbal appointment, and it is rare for a few families to use a red paper post. Relatives come first, and neighbors come the day before the official day. They sent a gift of two or four jiao, and very few have two yuan, supporting the old and carrying the young, the whole family came; moreover, they ate from breakfast to night meal. The wine feast on the previous day always uses fresh meat, half-cooked and non-crispy fresh fish, and the five internal organs in the pig's belly. Inside the house, on the ground, there are many tables densely arranged; large glasses of wine, large bowls of rice, gobbling, the bottom of the bowl facing the sky; not enough to eat, guests can also take a large bowl and add to the kitchen

The dishes on the official day are slightly more delicate. Although there are no valuable things such as shark fin and bird's nest, they will also invite famous and good chefs from the countryside to cook some stir-fries, such as sea cucumber chicken slices; there will also be coarse and sweet Babao rice for refreshments; some fruits and peanuts will also be placed on the corners of the table. This table is called the main banquet, and the people in the countryside also eat politely, but in the end, there is nothing left, and the soup is dry.

In the evening, men, women, old and young, crowded into a new house. The bride sits upright like the land grandmother in the temple, daring not to move or laugh. The bridegroom's face is red, and he is teased by a group of congratulatory guests who are full of wine. Laughing and making noise until three o'clock in the morning, the host took out things like peanuts, melon seeds, water chestnuts, and sugar cane to send them away.

Tomorrow, they will eat and drink all day like the day before. After two days, the wedding feast is over. The money spent by the host family is limited in other aspects, but just taking this food and drink as an example, it accounts for six or seven tenths of the expenditure.

The Last Dose of Medicine! 201

Records of Incense in the Air 202

— Original by Princess Der Ling of Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

The shoe uppers themselves were mostly made of the finest tribute satin, each in a different color. They were embroidered with various patterns using threads of different colors. These threads were dyed by the silk artisans, saving the expense of purchasing them from outside. However, the threads were so fine that simply by looking at them, one would immediately believe that the embroidery work on the shoe uppers was indeed extremely taxing on the eyes!

The heart of this shoe-making "factory" was the central main hall, filled with all sorts of tools, so many different kinds that I had never seen most of them before. Although I later asked the two old spinster leaders about each one, the names were so numerous and complex that I can't recall them all now. Every time I went there, I had to ask the two old spinsters to take out several pages of newly designed shoe patterns for me to look at. These shoe patterns were indeed very beautiful! To praise them in modern terms, they were truly exquisite drawings. I often admired them so much that I couldn't bear to put them down, wondering how the girls who created these patterns had learned such skills. Some of the drawings were exceptionally neat, looking like real shoes in the eyes of the viewer, as if one could simply take them down and wear them. Moreover, they weren't just monochrome sketches; they were colored drawings, with the colors of the shoe material and the patterns already rendered. When the shoes were eventually made, they would be exactly like the drawings on the paper, just like the sample books prepared by modern fashion companies. (292)

Little Xi Zai 203

— By Zhang Henshui

Chapter Twelve: Ashamed of Having No Clothes, Drawing the Curtain to Avoid Guests; Laboring Diligently to Save Lamp Oil, Copying Books at Dawn

Cheng Zhiqian was a person with very modern ideas. However, having come to a place like Xi'an, there were many things he had to be cautious about. A girl like Zhu Yueying came from a feudal society, where it was impossible for women to talk to men under normal circumstances. Now, only because she was desperately poor did she have to come forward and interact with men. Therefore, although he sympathized with her greatly, considering her helplessness, he didn't want to get too close to her. He thought that she must be suffering inwardly while putting on a facade for people. Thinking this way, he consistently maintained this attitude towards Yueying. Seeing Yueying forced by the wind and rain to fall directly into the mud, Yang Huanhua and Hu Saozi only shouted anxiously, unable to bend down to help her. Zhiqian really couldn't bear it any longer, so he rushed forward, regardless of the mud and rain, and jumped directly in front of Yueying. He bent down, grabbed her under the arms, lifted her up, and, supporting and pushing her, led her to the corridor. He said seriously, "You'll catch a cold easily. Quickly go to my room, take off your wet clothes, and ask the tea server to go home and get some clothes for you to change into. I'll wait for you here in the corridor." Yueying had fallen head over heels, already feeling ashamed. Being lifted up and helped to the corridor made her feel like a child. Her face immediately turned as red as pig's blood. Yang Huanhua and Hu Saozi also came over, and seeing her dripping wet, they couldn't help but frown. (181)

Humorous Dialogue 204

— (Ying Dai)

A: Zhang Jun and Ms. Li are engaged. What are your thoughts?

B: She got a diamond ring, and he took out another loan.

He Got Married

Diner: Didn't the advertisement say that you changed managers and reopened the old shop? But Dao is still the same old boss as before! I recognize him.

Waiter: Yes, sir! But he got married yesterday.

Where Travels Led

Quick Sketch of a Trip to Wuxi 205

— Xiaoci

Among all the counties in the country, Wuxi can be considered the most prosperous. Just looking at the actual situation of its industry and education can deeply convince one of this. Wuxi is not only a model county but also one of the famous scenic spots in the southeast. In the past, I only heard people praising it in this way, and I couldn't help but feel a sense of longing! Fortunately, this time, during the April 4th Children's Day, I was able to make a special trip to visit, staying for three days and enjoying the scenery before returning. The "Wuxi scenery" of lakes and mountains is indeed unique and worth appreciating and remembering.

I didn't investigate Wuxi's industry, nor did I visit its educational institutions. During this hurried trip, I only toured a few scenic spots. Wuxi's famous scenic spots can be categorized into four areas: (1) the Huishan Scenic Line, (2) the Lakeside Scenic Line, (3) the Urban Scenic Line, and (4) the Rural Scenic Line. This time, I focused on the Huishan and Lakeside areas. Although each of these four areas has its own unique flavor, in my opinion, the urban and rural areas are quite ordinary. The Huishan area is antique but too commercial, while only the Lakeside area, with its vast lakes and mountains and enduring spirit, is truly worth seeing.

The Lakeside area is particularly attractive because it is surrounded by mountains and faces Tai Lake. By arranging the scenery based on this natural landscape and adding artificial embellishments, it outshines other areas. Tai Lake is the third largest freshwater lake in our country, with rolling white waves and scattered islands. It has the famous Seventy-Two Peaks and a reported area of 36,000 hectares, showcasing its magnificent atmosphere. Yuantouzhu is the top scenic spot on the lakeside, with mountains, water, and gardens everywhere. Nearby are Ba Jiang Liao Lun's cliff inscriptions "Horizontal Clouds" and "Embracing Wu and Yue," which aptly describe Tai Lake. The scenery on Yuantouzhu Mountain is beautiful, needless to say. The Tai Lake Villa on the mountaintop faces the lake, and looking out from the heights, one can see the water and sky merging. This tranquil place even gave me a sense of being in paradise.

Leaving Yuantouzhu, I followed the circular lakeside road, reaching the newly built Baojie Bridge at the foot of Baojie Mountain. It spans the lake surface, entirely built of cement, with sixty-three arches, about three miles long, and costing hundreds of thousands. It is said to have been built with donations from the Rong family. About a mile from the bridge is "Li Garden," facing the Wuli Lake and overlooking Guangchang Creek. Its natural terrain and picturesque scenery make the garden's layout and arrangement no less beautiful than the "Ye Garden" in Jiangwan. From here to Meiyuan next to Dumu Mountain, I passed through more than ten miles of winding mountain paths. Sitting in a rickshaw, I was indeed a bit bored. Fortunately, the rural scenery was enough to give one a panoramic view, which was also a pleasant experience for city dwellers. Meiyuan was built by the Rong family. From the hillside to the summit, countless plum trees were planted, and the gentle breeze was incomparably cool. The garden has all sorts of pavilions and towers. At the summit are the Nianqu Pagoda, the Zongjing Villa, and his study. To the east is the Huoran Cave, carved out of the mountain, and the highest point is the golf course. Looking out at Tai Lake, the sails are like crows, offering a unique interest. On the mountainside is the Tai Lake Hotel, exclusively for tourists to stay. I also stayed for two nights this time. Living in the mountains was a first for me.

Wuxi is truly a place where outstanding people gather. Although it has beautiful natural lakes and mountains, without the Rong (Zongjing), Yang (Hanxi), and Wang (Yuqing) families' willingness to donate and manage, Wuxi would not have today's prosperity!

Shen Bao Radio Weekly

New Type of Carbon Resistor 208

— Yong Yan

There are commonly three types of fixed resistors in radio equipment. The first type is made of resistance wire wound around a core, the second type is a thin layer of carbon material coated on an insulating substrate, and the third type is the so-called "carbon fixed resistor," made of fine carbon particles mixed with an insulating powder. Among these three types, the first type is accurate and durable, but unfortunately, it is too expensive. The second type, due to manufacturing reasons, has too small a cross-sectional area and is only suitable for resistors that pass a small amount of current. Therefore, in practice, the third type, the carbon fixed resistor, is used most often and has the most potential for development. However, the carbon fixed resistors on the market are not accurate enough in resistance and are not very durable, which is not entirely satisfactory. This is why manufacturers are constantly researching and experimenting to improve their products.

American Lynck Mfg. Co. has now produced a new type of resistor that surpasses the old carbon resistor in both accuracy and durability.

It is said that the biggest reason for the inaccuracy and ease of damage in the old type lies in the inconsistent composition. This is because it is made by mixing fine carbon powder with an insulating material. The resistance is inversely proportional to the amount of carbon powder. The conductive part is only some carbon powder in the difficult-to-insulate material, so once subjected to external heat or shock, the position of the carbon powder inside easily changes, affecting the accuracy of the resistance. This explanation is supported by experiments. In experiments, when an excessive amount of current is passed through, and the interior is observed, starry sparks can be seen. These starry sparks are undoubtedly caused by the excessive current passing through the carbon powder and generating heat. In addition, a cross-sectional photograph of an old-style resistor magnified eighty times under a microscope clearly shows that its surface is granular and porous. Of course, if the surface is not dense, it is easily attacked by moisture, which changes its resistance.

Based on the above results, the raw materials and manufacturing steps of the new type of resistor have been completely reformed. The raw material is made by mixing two kinds of powders with different resistivity. The ratio of these two powders determines the resistance. Therefore, the conductive part is no longer limited to carbon powder as in the old type. During manufacturing, it is thoroughly mixed and then formed into a strip under extreme pressure to ensure its uniform composition and dense surface. In tests, such products, even when subjected to an excessive amount of current, do not generate starry sparks like the old type. At the same time, a cross-section magnified eighty times shows that its surface is much denser. Therefore, the new type of product is much better than the old type. Although it cannot be said to have reached the ideal standard, it is not far off. The following are some comparisons from several experiments:

When the new type is subjected to twice the specified power, or even four times the specified power, its resistance usually changes by only slightly less than one percent, and the maximum is only two percent. It is also not damaged in boiling water. In another experiment, at a temperature of 135 degrees Fahrenheit, carrying the specified power for 350 hours, the resistance did not change, even when the actual temperature rose to 193 degrees (due to I2R loss). However, in the old type, it had changed by about 4 to 10 percent. (The rest is omitted to save space.) In addition, under the Cathode Ray Test, the new type does not emit noise during use. Furthermore, the contact point between the body of the new resistor and the pigtail has also been improved, so the contact is more perfect than the old type.

Knowledge That Beginning Comrades Should Possess (Continued, Part 2) 209

— Yang Xuelun

(6) Circuit: Once the components are purchased, assembly can begin. Start with a three-circuit regenerative receiver because it is simple to wire, has few components, and has excellent efficiency. Use 37 or 38 for vacuum tubes for AC, and 30 or 33 for DC. The second step is to add one or two stages of low-frequency amplification, using transformer or resistor coupling. Although the volume of resistor coupling is not as good as that of the transformer, the position occupied by the resistor is economical, the amplification is uniform, and there is no frequency dependence, so it is often used. After you have mastered the low-frequency amplification assembly, you will have gained considerable knowledge and experience. Then, the third step is to add one or two stages of high-frequency amplification, using a tuned radio frequency (t.r.f.) circuit. After this machine is completed, its selectivity, sensitivity, and volume are definitely more than enough for amateur home use.

(7) Assembly Method: Arranging components and soldering wires are important tasks in assembling a radio. It is common to see beginners whose wiring is correct but fail because they have not soldered the wires properly. The high-frequency and detection coils must not be placed in the same magnetic field. It is best to place them at right angles to each other or isolate them with an aluminum shield. In addition, when winding coils, they must be tight and uniform, and the wiring of the screen grids and diodes must be short and not parallel. At the beginning of assembling the wooden box and base, you can reserve space for expansion to avoid having to reassemble everything in the future. It is up to you whether to install the speaker in a wooden box or not. In my opinion, it is better to install the power supply part of the AC radio in a separate wooden box, because it can also be used for other experiments.

(8) Power Transformer: It is best for amateurs to make their own power transformers or have them custom-made by a manufacturer. The secondary output, B+, is best wound to 500 volts, 1 amp, with a center tap for full-wave rectification. A+ should be wound with 1.5 volts, 3.5 amps, 5 volts, 2 amps, and 6.3 volts, 1.5 amps, three coils, all connected to the center line. As for the design methods for the number of turns of the coils, the gauge of the wire, and the cross-sectional area of the iron core, they are all recorded in various newspapers and magazines, so I won't repeat them here. The A+ transformer used in semi-AC models can be purchased as a doorbell transformer with a 6-volt secondary coil, but the doorbell transformer does not have a center line. You can remove it and rewind it, or connect a 50 to 75 ohm center resistor in parallel.

Having written this, I must make a final statement and solemnly advise the readers that nowadays, cheap and inferior goods flood the market. Those unscrupulous merchants have exhausted their conscience and are only interested in profit. We amateurs must not be insane and greedy for cheapness, lest we be ridiculed for having a five-minute craze. (End)

Skip Distance of Shortwave Communication (Continued) 210

— Chong Ling

(2) Elevation Angle of Radio Waves: Radio waves are radiated upwards to the Heaviside layer and reflected back to the ground. However, not all radio waves with various elevation angles can be reflected back by the Heaviside layer. In fact, when the elevation angle of a certain wavelength exceeds a certain angle, it can directly penetrate the Heaviside layer and never return. Therefore, for each wavelength, under certain conditions of the Heaviside layer, there is only a maximum elevation angle. Beyond this angle, the radio waves are consumed outside the Heaviside layer and cannot be reflected back. This maximum elevation angle, except for those close to ninety degrees, reflects radio waves that are very far from the transmitting station, so the skip distance is inevitable. As shown in Figure 1, it is clear that the skip distance increases as the elevation angle decreases. The shorter the wavelength, the smaller the maximum elevation angle, so the skip distance also increases. According to Taylor's report on the maximum elevation angle: in the spring, for the Heaviside layer at 1000 miles, the elevation angle is 54 degrees for a 40-meter wavelength and 18 degrees for a 20-meter wavelength. In the winter night, for the Heaviside layer at 500 miles, it is 52 degrees for 40 meters, and 0 degrees for a 10-meter wavelength.

(3) Height of the Heaviside Layer: The height of the Heaviside layer rises and falls with the seasons and day and night. It has a slight impact on the elevation angle of radio waves and has a large relationship with changes in wavelength. It is higher in winter than in summer, and lower during the day than at night. It is lowest in late summer, about 50 to 100 miles, and highest in winter nights, 300 to 500 miles. Summer nights are 150 to 220 miles, and winter days are only 100 to 170 miles. As the height of the Heaviside layer increases, the skip distance also increases accordingly. This can be seen from Figure 2. (End)

Introducing the Philips Wireless Radio Magazine 211

Philips Wireless Radio Magazine is published by Philips Foreign Company at 133 Sichuan Road, Shanghai. It specializes in describing various wireless radio theories and manufacturing methods in the most accessible and fluent language and introduces the latest theories from Europe and the United States. Therefore, although it has only been published for half a year, the number of long-term subscribers has increased to more than 10,000, making it the most popular wireless radio magazine in our country. I am honored to have received a complimentary copy of the ninth issue of the first volume published today. Inside, there is an article on the manufacturing method of a two-tube battery radio, from winding the coil to how to start using the entire machine after it is made. The manufacturing of the chassis, the component arrangement method, and the wiring procedures are all described in great detail in a very accessible language that even children can read. There are also 25 detailed illustrations explaining how to install a screw and how to connect a wire. By reading it, you can immediately start manufacturing. Other valuable contents include a short essay on wireless radio and the standardization of wireless radio terms, which are worth reading. It is said that the price is very cheap, only 15 cents per issue, and 12 issues per year are only $1.50. Those who mention that they were introduced by this newspaper can be exempted from postage.
