Virgin Insurance 212

— Meng Ruo

Hong Kong News: In the islands of the Dutch East Indies in the South Seas, there is an island named Ba Boss, where women are not allowed to leave the island. Even when going out for a daily stroll, they must cover their faces with a black cloth, leaving only their eyes to see. Now, a Westerner named Mr. Yunzhe has deposited more than 100,000 yuan with the island's government as a security deposit to obtain permission to take more than 20 famous dancers from the area to travel the world and perform. They are scheduled to arrive in Hong Kong at the end of next month. It is also said that these more than 20 dancers are all virgins. When they return to the island in the future, they must undergo a physical examination by a doctor to see if there have been any changes, before the security deposit can be reclaimed. Otherwise, it will be confiscated. Therefore, the Westerner has specially hired an island woman and two Western women to closely monitor them day and night to prevent any mishaps that could lead to a complete loss.

The fate of the women of Ba Boss Island seems extremely unfortunate! Not being allowed to leave the island deprives them of the freedom of movement that people should have! Even when going out for a daily stroll, they must cover their faces with a black cloth, leaving only their eyes to see. This is simply not treating them as human beings!

However, there are exceptions after all. Now, the Westerner Mr. Yunzhe has taken out more than 100,000 yuan as a security deposit, and the government has made an exception and released more than 20 dancers to travel the world. Money can make gods work, and this is indeed not a false statement!

However, the island's government, which usually controls local women so strictly, still cannot feel at ease even though they have released these more than 20 dancers. Because these dancers are all virgins, the authorities, to protect the dignity of their virginity, came up with a clever method and signed a treaty with the Westerner, stipulating that when the dancers return to the island in the future, they must undergo a physical examination by a doctor to see if there have been any changes before the security deposit can be reclaimed, otherwise, it will be confiscated. This strategy is indeed foolproof. The Westerner, in order to protect his more than 100,000 yuan investment, specially hired an island woman and two Western women to closely monitor them day and night to prevent any mishaps. This is tantamount to the island's government entrusting him with the responsibility of controlling these more than 20 virgins.

But we really don't understand why the government of this Ba Boss Island restricts ordinary women so much? Why does it value virgins so much? Who is this for? Naturally, it is for the men! Otherwise, they wouldn't take such measures.

However, it is strange that virgins are precious, but money is even more precious! Although the authorities of Ba Boss Island value virgins very much, as long as there is money, virgins can also be sold! Otherwise, doesn't the phrase "otherwise, it will be confiscated" clearly state that if these dancers' bodies have changed after the examination, the more than 100,000 yuan security deposit will be confiscated, and that's the end of it?

Rain 213

— Simon

I praise the rain. I can't forget all the scenes it has left in my memory, and I like to trace them with a kind of delicate emotion. Rain has the potential to change your mood and is even more suitable for the indulgence of a person who is accustomed to a solitary life. It can drive away all the vulgar disturbances outside your world and create a quiet realm beyond compare, making you forget everything that exists except yourself. But its diverse, beautiful patterns and profound meanings are not something everyone can appreciate. It is truly like an obscure poem that cannot be fully understood without careful eyes. Perhaps it is when a large dark cloud suddenly appears in the sky at dusk, and the sky gradually darkens. You think that the rain is probably coming, and as you are thinking this, the rain is already drizzling lightly. Then, it falls harder and harder, and in an instant, the ground, the roof tiles, and the leaves are all wet.

Page 22

Wettened. You lean on the window and stare. Before long, the distant scenery that was just brightly reflected in your eyes is also shrouded in a heavy mist, blurred like a layer of smoke. Even the intertwined images of people coming and going in the street outside the window are equally submerged in the misty rain, and almost nothing can be seen because the windowpanes are covered with raindrops. Then, the sky completely darkens. Only the gradually dripping rain can be heard, becoming the only solo piece in the dusk. In this way, your mood will inevitably change very quickly. Just as the rain changes the outside world, if you were planning to go out before the rain, but the rain is already dripping endlessly, and the road is muddy, who would be happy to run out again? Change the time. Suddenly, you will dispel the idea of going out and sit down peacefully. Whether to go or not is not something you need to hesitate about. The rain is falling so steadily that it won't stop immediately. Usually, you can't avoid being indecisive, but at this moment, you absolutely don't need to worry about these things. You have only one thought: don't go. Even if there is something important, the person you are supposed to meet may have already guessed that you won't come, or they may have given up waiting and are deciding for you that you don't need to go. Rain will invisibly give you some peace and comfort. If you want to be quiet the most, this is the quietest time. Rain prevents people from visiting you, so you don't have to worry about unexpected disturbances. Just focus on thinking what you want to think and doing what you want to do.

In the middle of the night, perhaps the continuous rain is even heavier. You sit alone by the bright lamp, surrounded by the silent, tombstone-like stillness. All that surrounds you is the dripping rain outside. You listen attentively to the eaves of rain dripping together and falling one after another. Lightly, heavily, one after the other, it sounds even crisper and more clanging, as if it penetrates from the depths of your heart, and even your soul seems to be immersed in it. You feel a strange sense of softness and a kind of pure beauty, like a clear lake with a visible bottom, and your body is like a dust-free swallow, inserting its wings and flying to the ideal country. You forget all the sorrows in your heart and the constraints of the coarse fabric of life. Rain can truly give you a selfless illusion and the liberation of spiritual shackles. And this gift is something anyone can seek. There is rain, rain is falling, and it is always and everywhere available. However, people who cannot bear the true beauty of rain are different. For them, rain becomes a hateful thing, especially if it keeps raining for days without end. There is no clean place except for the house. How can they not be annoyed, reducing the scope of daily life to just one house? People who are good at moving and wandering mostly curse the rain, because rain will ruthlessly extinguish all their interests outside. And it's no wonder that they can't have a connection with rain.

The Story of Mr. Nice Guy 214

— Jiang Tian

The dilapidated temple, surrounded by weeds on all sides, used to be a place of great incense and popularity. People from the town and nearby villages would come to draw a fortune stick on the first and fifteenth of each month because the fortune sticks here were extremely accurate, with about nine out of ten being correct. Therefore, the incense became more and more prosperous day by day.

But in just two years, this place had completely changed. Not only did no one from the nearby villages come to the temple, but not even a single person from the town came. The temple keeper understood the reason for this, but he always wondered why this sacred deity, who used to be so efficacious, was no longer worshipped? Even if the harvest was bad, and natural and man-made disasters had led to family ruin and death, they should still pray to the gods. What were these people thinking?

The temple keeper stubbornly guarded the temple for two years, hoping that it would flourish again. Even if it couldn't return to its former glory, at least someone should come to the temple! But the temple keeper's hope was shattered day by day, finally leading to his disappointment. He couldn't stay in this dilapidated temple, which hadn't been repaired for two years, and live with an empty stomach. He had no choice but to abandon this land of opportunity and go elsewhere to seek a livelihood.

The temple was already dilapidated, but after the temple keeper left, it became even more desolate. Weeds grew wildly on all sides, uneven and rampant. The sacred place, once bustling with incense, had become a desolate ruin.

For several months, no one had lived there. The weeds grew so tall that they covered the temple gate. Inside the temple, a foul odor permeated the air, and spiderwebs covered the deity's seat, making it airtight. The ash on the seat was already an inch thick.

This dilapidated temple was almost forgotten in people's minds. In this era, no one would come to the temple to burn incense anymore. However, this suited Mr. Nice Guy perfectly. He could move into this dilapidated temple without attracting attention. He had been living here for over a month now.

There was only one public elementary school and one private school in the town. The private school had closed its doors two years ago. The public school had managed to persevere, but it finally had to close this year. However, a notice was posted at the entrance, saying that it was temporarily suspending classes for one semester. But who would believe that? In such a depressed market, who would still study, and who could afford to donate money to the school? It would be fortunate enough if the shops didn't close!

Mr. Xu was an honest man who had been teaching in the town for over a decade. He wasn't a local. He had come here over a decade ago to work as a secretary in the district office. At that time, he was around forty years old. After working as a secretary in the district office for a few years, he was invited to teach in the public school. Because he was honest and older, no matter how the school's administrators changed, and the teachers were renewed every year, only he had never been moved. He continued to teach year after year. Everyone knew that he was the most knowledgeable person in the town, and the students he taught were all knowledgeable and reasonable.

Mr. Xu gradually became famous in the town. The students in the school liked him because he taught well and was honest. He had a naturally quiet personality, and he was very slow to do things. No one had ever seen him in a hurry. Now that he was older, he had become an even more mature, prudent, and peaceful Mr. Nice Guy. Almost everyone in the town knew that he was a Mr. Nice Guy.

However, things often don't go as planned. From two years ago until now, the town's economy had been deteriorating day by day. Not to mention that parents from the villages didn't send their children to school, even in the town, except for a few wealthier families, no one had money to send their children to school. Gradually, the school became deserted. This year, it had to close due to a lack of funding.

Once the school closed, Mr. Nice Guy had no way to make a living. At first, he could still live in the empty school, but recently it had been rented out to store goods. The issue of housing caused Mr. Nice Guy to panic.

After searching for several days, he finally found this dilapidated temple, which shared the same fate as the school.

From then on, he lived in this forgotten temple, but he was still thinking:

"As long as the harvest is better, and the school reopens, I will be a teacher again."

However, this hope ultimately wouldn't come to pass.

Page 23

Night on the Banks of the Chao Phraya River 215

— Jing Yun

The sun slants to the west, floating on the scarlet Chao Phraya River, collecting its scorching flames, as big as a copper gong, the reddest like the yolk of a salted duck egg, quietly sinking into the rippling water.

At this time, the azure blue sky is covered with shimmering evening clouds, reflecting thousands of golden waves on the Chao Phraya River, like an endless serpent, gently rippling. The beautiful and serene scenery of the southern country evening is so beautiful and pleasing!

On both banks of the Chao Phraya River, the "Ti Tou" (a "Ti Tou" is slightly smaller than a pier, serving the same purpose, and is made of teak wood) is gradually becoming more crowded with people - some foreign vagrants adrift! They have finished their hard and heavy work from the day, eaten dinner, and are whistling a seductive southern tune, carefree, carrying iron buckets bare-chested on the riverbank to enjoy the cool air. Naturally, the topic of their conversations at this time is those flirtatious and beautiful "foreign" girls with their bare upper bodies, exposing two sharp, towering breasts like newly built graves.

"Bingxing, after we cool off, let's go to Triangle Street together for an iced coffee," the young man Yu Agou, bending over, scoops a bucket of water from the river and pours it over his head in a flurry, turning his head to Bingxing, who is whistling so cheerfully. "Then let's go to 'Sky Beyond the Sky' to listen to the opera. A new female Dan (female role) has arrived. Her dark, sparkling eyes glance down the stage, quite pretty! I'll be the host, will you go?..."

The young fellow called Bingxing didn't respond, just kept scooping water from the river with his iron bucket, pouring it over his head in a torrent, whistling a passionate and unrestrained tune.

"What's wrong? Are you going to 'Sky Beyond the Sky' to listen to the opera?... Or is that 'foreign' girl behind the hostel making you crazy!" Yu Agou hits his arm, pretending to be very angry.

"Humph, humph... Agou, I'm really sorry! I have something to do tonight."

Everyone knows that Bingxing is the kind of guy who loves to hang out with "foreign girls" and go to the opera house. Usually, as soon as the sun sinks into the Chao Phraya River, his soul is taken by them. Why is it that tonight, when he is invited to go out, he insists he has something to do? This makes Yu Agou feel a little uncomfortable! However, he is too embarrassed to force him again. So, he examines Bingxing's face for a while and laughs nasally!

"Humph,... you rascal, go on your way! I know you have a date with that 'foreign' girl tonight. I know! Humph... Agou makes a face at him for a while, then, carrying the iron bucket, leaves the "Ti Tou" with a thud.

Bingxing dries the dampness from his body, puts on his clothes, and strolls leisurely along the riverbank until he reaches the "Royal Ti Tou," where he stops and stares blankly at the heart of the river, lost in thought. "She should be coming about now," Bingxing thinks, lowering his head.

"Bingxing, you must have been waiting anxiously, right? I'm really sorry!" The girl's voice is soft, gentle, like a singing nightingale.

Instantly, Bingxing's heart is happy, his face like a spring rose. At this moment, his heart blossoms!

"Lina, why are you so late? The moon has already crept up to the treetops of the coconut grove!"

They sit closely shoulder to shoulder on the "Ti Tou," looking at the quiet river water like silk, whispering intimately.

Apart from their tender, soft conversation, sharp laughter, and the crisp, clear sounds of fish leaping out of the calm water and then falling back in from time to time, everything lies silently under the moonlight. The night on the banks of the Chao Phraya River is so poetic, cool, and serene!

Before and After Returning Home 216

— Chong Lin

(I)

On the first night on the "Da Da Niang" ship, I lay wearily in the cabin, silently exhaling a few long breaths. Good, all the chaos before departure had ended, and both I and my luggage had been safely moved onto the ship. If our ship didn't catch fire in the ocean like the "George Philip," then we could patiently wait to see our Shanghai.

But a new uneasiness, anxiety, and worry arose in my mind. The China of my long-held dreams, I was about to see it. Could this be real? It was real. I couldn't help but laugh, but my laughter immediately brought sorrow. So the matter of returning home became something that seemed necessary but unwelcome.

The night before arriving in Singapore, I was enjoying the cool air on deck. A grassy scent—the scent of oriental grass—drifted from the islands on both sides, suddenly like a shot of anesthetic into my brain, stirring deep homesickness in me.

On the Singapore pier, I saw a fashionable Chinese Miss—or Madam—who had come to see someone off. Her clothes were in a style I hadn't imagined for years: a long silk dress, with slits up to her thighs, short sleeves, a high, stiff collar, and her hair was permed, with high heels. But as I looked at her closely, seeing her clenched arms and stooped, unstraight back, I couldn't help but feel uncomfortable and uneasy for her. I couldn't help but want to say to her:

"Straighten your back, why are you clenching your arms? Be more natural! Be more energetic!"

A Mr. Wang, who was studying sculpture on the same ship, was unlike the usual Chinese artist, had some practical thoughts, and his criticism of things was sometimes very close to ours. He began to sigh with emotion

"Chinese people just love that kind of affectation. I'm used to seeing naked human bodies, but I don't find it obscene. The way Chinese women dress now, with their long dresses slit up to their thighs, is really obscene."

"Really, if you want to expose your thighs to the sun, then you might as well make the dress shorter." (To be continued)

Amateur Mailbox

Is "Coal" a Plant? 217

Editor Sir:

Recently, in your column, I saw your description of "The Production and Uses of Petroleum," which was concise and to the point, providing us shop assistants with no scientific knowledge with a lot of academic help. I am truly grateful.

Page 24

Page 25

Due to "Petroleum," I am writing to ask you about a problem that has been hidden in my mind for a long time. I think that since you are willing to explain petroleum in such detail, you probably won't refuse my question, right?

There is something that is widely used, and it is an indispensable thing in industry, that is, "coal," which everyone knows. We can be said to see "coal" every day, black things one by one, which are not unusual at all. However, if you use a scholar's attitude to investigate, it makes me unable to answer my question. For example: is coal like a plant, growing out of the ground? What is it made of? Or is there another reason? Therefore, I have asked others, but others cannot clearly answer these questions. Finally, I have no choice but to trouble you. I think you will definitely give me some guidance.

Also: are "stone coal" and "coal" two different things? Yours respectfully, Yang Kaisheng

Editor's Note: "Coal" is indeed a very common substance, and there must be many people who know how it is produced, which is not surprising. But based on the general level of knowledge of the public, we believe that there must be many people whose understanding of "coal" is very vague. Therefore, we will briefly describe it as follows.

"Coal" is the common name for "stone coal." Speaking of the causes of these coals, it was a matter of ancient times. In very ancient times, the temperature inside the earth was much higher than it is now, and the seawater at that time was heated by the high temperature. This hot sea increased the temperature in the air, and dew and water vapor filled the atmosphere; at the same time, the carbon dioxide contained in the atmosphere was also more than it is now, so it could make plants flourish. People now call that era the Carboniferous Period, the era when ferns flourished. The speed at which plants grew at that time was beyond our imagination. It is said that the seeds of plants fell on the ground and sprouted immediately. Before long, they grew into large trees, and then the large trees fell and died. Young plants continued to flourish one after another. After the ground was covered with the remains and seeds of the fallen plants, the plants that grew each died and were piled on top of them again. These plant remains gradually overlapped, reaching hundreds or thousands of feet in thickness: after this thick layer of plant remains mostly sank to the bottom of the sea, mud and sand pressed on it, gradually accumulating, also reaching thousands of feet in thickness. After tens of thousands of years, the plant remains buried deep in the ground gradually changed. The "hydrogen" and "oxygen" in the plant components gradually disappeared, (leaving behind) carbonaceous matter, which became today's coal.

Coal has anthracite, bituminous coal, lignite, and peat. Anthracite is the highest-grade coal, which does not produce coal smoke when burned. The chemical changes of this coal have mostly ended, and it is almost entirely carbon coal. The following order of bituminous coal, lignite, and peat is gradually lower, especially peat. Because the chemical changes of peat have not yet been completed, it contains a lot of "hydrogen" and "oxygen", and it does not burn much when burned? It also produces a lot of smoke.

Also, that coal tar made from coal through dry distillation can be used to make various dyes and medicines and is also an important material in industry. Due to space limitations, let's talk about it next time if we have the opportunity.

Classical Chinese 221

Wang Bingmei Donglai Bo Yi

Huaxing (1260) 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM

Qi, Zheng, and Wei Fight at Lang (Continued)

Alas, if a small country has merit and can step on top of a large country, then a minister has merit and can override his ruler, and a son has merit and can be proud of his father. I once saw Zheng Hu at the beginning when he defeated the Rong army, imprisoned the two commanders, displayed the captives, and presented them to Qi in triumph, his spirit swallowing the feudal lords, looking down on the nobility. At the time of the gift, he was temporarily taken by someone first, and when he mobilized the armies of the three countries to attack him, how magnificent it was. When he succeeded to the throne, he was weak and did not flourish. His exile, his return, repudiating his name and going to the feudal lords, and even slandering him as a cunning child, they did not treat him as a ruler at the meeting. Suffering such humiliation, where was the magnificence of the past? The reason is that Hu's personality is that when he is successful, his spirit is full, and he regards himself as not being able to bear its greatness. People slightly despise him, and he cannot calm down. When he is frustrated, his spirit dries up, and he regards himself as not being able to bear its smallness. People greatly despise him, but he cannot compare. In it, there is no master at the beginning, only looking at external objects as light or heavy, filling with things, drying up with things, becoming big with things, becoming small with things. Sometimes arrogant and sometimes discouraged, sometimes brave and sometimes timid, he cannot even know himself. If he cannot control himself, how can he master the country?

Shen Bao Local Supplement Film Special

Literary Works are Sprouting Up, and Dickens Has Become a Cash Cow 223

— Zhu Heng

When film merchants find that glamorous, sensual song and dance films with big legs and frightening war beast films are no longer popular with audiences, their business eyes turn to literary works. Their business sense is indeed good, and they are indeed shifting their strategy based on "economics." Isn't it so? Filming literary works naturally ensures reliable sales, because the content of the subject matter is already familiar to everyone. With such an advertising foundation, filming will naturally create a sensation. Of course, film producers also have their captivating rhetoric, which is to enhance the audience's literary interest and appreciation of literary works.

There have been many literary works adapted for the screen, and everyone knows the names, so I won't list them again. What I want to describe now is Mr. Dickens. I think this gentleman can be considered the most valuable cash cow for film merchants today. Because his novels have been popular for decades, and the scope of readers is the widest. Based on this reason, they immediately concluded and echoed in unison, "It will definitely make money."

You see, his works that have been filmed and seen by people in Shanghai include "Oliver Twist," starring American child star Dickie Moore, "Great Expectations," produced by Universal Company and starring Phillip Holmes, and "A Tale of Two Cities," which is currently being screened. The Universal Company is currently filming the mysterious "The Mystery of Edwin Drood." This film stars Claude Rains, and most of the actors are British. Dickens's novel is full of suspense. According to Universal personnel, the success of this film in the future will definitely be a hit, because this film is Universal's greatest horror film since Lon Chaney's "The Hunchback of Notre Dame."

"The Old Curiosity Shop" is being filmed in the British Hollywood—Elstree. The director of this film is the famous British Dickens expert Thomas Bentley. He once specialized in playing characters from Dickens's books on the British stage and won praise.

Two works are being prepared for filming: "A Tale of Two Cities" and "The Pickwick Papers." American and British companies are discussing filming these two novels. According to recent news, Warner Bros. has decided to film "The Pickwick Papers" with the great character actor Guy Kibbee playing Mr. Pickwick. Britain has also decided to produce this film. It may be on the market earlier than the American film. Let's wait and see which one is better.

This year can be said to be "Dickens Year" in the British and American film circles. However, when literary films are once again disliked by audiences, where will the film merchants' business eyes turn?

Film Review

Review of "Rainbow Rhythm" 224

— You Jing

Aunty Sally - Guang Lu Screening

The comedy song and dance film "Rainbow Rhythm" is just like its theme song "Spring Clouds and Rainbows," something like clouds, haze, rainbows, just illusory, fictional, and unreasonable coincidences.

In order to point out these shortcomings, I must first briefly describe its plot: Kelly, the king of a New York nightclub, ran to London to open a large-scale nightclub in order to escape the harassment of local gangsters. He used the song and dance program "Spring Clouds and Rainbows" as a gimmick for the opening ceremony. When hundreds of girls applied for training, Sally, who claimed to have performance talent, suddenly came and pestered him to join the performance in a seemingly crazy manner. After being rejected several times, she threw herself into Kelly's home and worked as a maid. Although he gradually changed from disliking her to liking her, he never agreed to her request to dedicate herself to song and dance.

Sally disguised herself as Sasha, a famous French singer, to see Kelly, and was indeed hired as the protagonist. During the makeup session before the performance, she was kidnapped by the previous gangsters. The play became tense in terms of the gangsters and Kelly bargaining, and Sally's attempts to escape from the bandit's den. As a result, she escaped back and rushed to perform the protagonist's play, and killed the bandit who murdered Kelly during the performance, and was "gratefully" married by him as his wife. Naturally, good is rewarded with good, and evil people such as gangsters will of course get their due evil results and fall into the clutches of the law.

Not only is the ending of good and evil being rewarded, and the happy ending is mediocre and ordinary, but the entire fictional story is so unreasonable! In fact, one who can win the title of king of nightclubs like Kelly should normally be a tycoon among gangsters, but here he is a cowardly weakling, and he can actually keep himself clean—as in the play, he is unwilling to associate with gangsters—this is unreasonable one. Kelly didn't recognize Sally, the maid who seemed crazy, repeatedly bothered him, and saw each other day and night, because she put on makeup. Instead, he regarded her as a real famous French singer Sasha, and gave her the position of protagonist, this is unreasonable two. Similarly, the person who played Sally's supporting role in the so-called "tumbling dance" was temporarily disguised by bandits and took the stage, and was able to perform the tumbling so well as shown in the play without being recognized by Kelly or the people in charge backstage, this is unreasonable three. As for the coincidences such as Sally escaping from the underground house, and a machine bicycle being driven back, and the costumed supporting actor happened to be knocked unconscious by the bandits at the door and stole his clothes to disguise himself, there are too many to enumerate.

On the other hand, the fact that London and New York are equally rampant with gangsters, and that kidnapping and assassinations can occur in public, is an exposure: and the satire that today is a maid, and tomorrow she can pretend to be a star, and actually achieve fame and success, is quite revealed.

Lim Whelan has worked extremely hard in directing this script written by Xian himself. Not only did he use many choreographic song and dance scenes, such as clouds and rainbows, to make the audience temporarily forget the dissatisfaction with reality, and Kelly's bargaining under the gangsters' guns, and the tense atmosphere of the song and dance performance and Sally's escape, the editing was extremely successful.

However, Xi Xuelei, known as the female Chaplin, has a kind of pretentious acting that makes people unable to compliment her. Of course, she also performed the two personalities after pretending to be Sally and the energy of a famous singer.

A scene from "Spring Breeze and Autumn Rain": "The First Love of the Child; The Lover of the Mother!" Performed by Lu Jier Herson and Warren William - Nanjing Screening

"Rainbow Rhythm" is the latest song and dance blockbuster from the British Gaodui Company. Starring the female Chaplin, Xi Xuelei Zhedena, the whole film is full of humorous and funny atmosphere. Today, it will be screened at Guangyi Cinema.

Xi Rendailisi can perform Chinese drama and is known as the foreign Mei Lanfang. She will meet the people of Shanghai soon.

Movie novel

Amateur Reporter (After Office Hours) (9) 225

— Tong Yun

Jordan's attitude when speaking was very stern. He continued, "I have warned you several times before, especially about your attitude towards my friends. But this time you have gone too far." Sharon, hearing Jordan reprimanding Jim Brown, raised her head unconsciously, with a very triumphant look on her face. She said to Jordan, "Goodbye. I'm leaving. My mother is still waiting for me at the Sunter Seaside Club." She said triumphantly and walked out, ignoring Jim.

After Sharon left, Jim said to Jordan, "Look, don't worry. I'll just resign." He said and walked out. When Barr and Gabe heard that Jim Brown had resigned, they also wanted to resign together, but Jim told them, "You have to stay here, you can't leave. None of you can leave. When I find the news, you can write it down right away." After he finished speaking, he left the newspaper office.

Jim left the newspaper office and ran straight to the Sunter Seaside Club to find Sharon. When he found her, his attitude was very humble. He said that he knew he had done something wrong and had now been dismissed from his job, and would soon be returning to Kansas City. "But the first thing I want to do," he said, "is to apologize to Tom Penisteder. But he won't talk to me on the phone. So I have to ask you. You just need to say one word, and he will be willing to see me."

Sharon believed his words and agreed. When they got into the car and headed towards Penisteder's house, Sharon was no longer as arrogant as before. She originally had a revengeful heart, wanting to watch Jim Brown reap his own reward. But now that Jim was about to leave New York and go to Kansas, she suddenly felt an inexplicable discomfort. She had forgotten how he had used everything about her. She felt a pang of pity for him, although in fact, he didn't seem to have any love for her.

When they arrived at Penisteder's door, Sharon felt a pang of discomfort in her heart that she could hardly bear. But Jim walked into Penisteder's house and didn't apologize to Penisteder either. He wandered around looking around. Sharon also forgave him, knowing that admitting guilt to others was a very embarrassing thing, so he was slow to open his mouth. At this time, Penisteder suddenly asked, "Sharon, I'm not being rude, but I want to know what Mr. Brown is here for?"

Sharon glanced at Jim and murmured. "Um... Ah... The truth is like this..." Brown glared at her, as if telling her not to speak. So he said himself: "I came to your house because I wanted to tell you that I was too much, I heard the rumors outside, and I believed it was true. It's just that someone said that Zhuliya Boderson had paid 200,000 yuan in bank loans for you, but I believed it. He pretended to tap his head with his finger and said: "I am really foolish."

Penisteder smiled slightly. Sharon's heart gradually became suspicious, feeling that Jim's words didn't sound like an apology, and his attitude was no longer as humble as before. But Jim continued to ramble: "I also thought... maybe last night, you rocked Zhulia Boderson to her house. Don't you have a small boat? But this is all your fault, let me guess wildly like this. Why didn't you tell me where you were last night?" (To be continued)
